Wang Shijian
§YBorn:§! §L1911, in Wendeng, Shandong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWang Shijian began his political career as a Chinese syndicalist ordered to help organise a secret radio station to rally Nationalist and socialist propaganda against the Zhili and their Manchu allies. He quickly rose up the ranks to become a party secretary of the Hebei Provincial Anti-Imperialist League, a peripheral organisation of the League of Chinese Syndicalists. As the Kuomintang and LCS lack a major presence in the Chinese Central Plains, Wang was a quick choice for a candidate to participate in Zhou Enlai's newly founded Zhongyang Teke.§!
Kang Sheng
§YBorn:§! §LNovember 4th, 1898, in Dataizhuang, Zhucheng County, Shandong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAs a young child, Kang Sheng was educated at a German school in Qingdao, earning him a eternal hatred for the German Empire. After graduating from the German school, Kang taught in a rural school in Zhucheng before leaving for Shanghai in 1924. In Shanghai, he enrolled in Shanghai University, then led by the Chinese Syndicalist Party - and then he joined the Youth League of the CSP. After formally joining the party, he participated in the February 1925 strike that culminated in the May 30th Movement and he also participated in the reorganisation of the CSP into the League of Chinese Syndicalists.\n\nAfter the failure of the Northern Expedition, Kang remained in China as a labour organiser and security operative of the LCS. He married fellow Shandong native Cao Yi'ou and entered the employment of Yu Qiaqing - whose connections with the Kuomintang helped put Kang in contact with the KMT. After the KMT's return to China, Kang was approached by Zhou Enlai to head internal security operations of the newly created Zhongyang Teke in Shandong. It is here in Shandong where Kang has earned an infamous reputation as a sadistic interrogator, with his methods arousing the frustration of the Party's Central Committee and of Zhou Enlai. He is known for accusing fellow LCS and even KMT members of harbouring German sympathies and once they confessed under heavy torture - would lead to an avalanche of arrests and purges.§!
Hu Chunpu
§YBorn:§! §L1913, in Qu, Sichuan Province, Republic of China§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAfter studying Sanhui Town Primary School, Hu Chunpu enrolled in Qu County Middle School in 1927 around the time, the Northern Expedition collapsed. In the summer of 1931, he was admitted to Shanghai Private School where he became involved with syndicalist-inspired student led activities. In February of 1935, he was introduced to the Chinese Syndicalist Party and became a member of the organisation. Due to his background in Sichuan, he was approached by Zhou Enlai to head a new branch of the Zhongyang Teke in Sichuan.§!
Wu Hongbin
§YBorn:§! §L1903, in Tianshui, Gansu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWu Hongbin is of Hui ethnicity and enrolled in 1923 to study law at Peking University, where he became influenced by the revolutionary mood of the university and joined the Chinese Syndicalist Party in 1926. He was appointed as Secretary of the Xicheng District Committee of the CSP under the direction of the League of Chinese Syndicalists and after graduating in 1929, went to teach in Yan'an. Due to his ethnic background as a Hui, he was a natural candidate to head the revolutionary security activities of the Zhongyang Teke in China's northwest provinces.§!

CFHI
The CFHI or China First Heavy Industry Group Co. Ltd, is a large scale equipment manufacturer in China. Managed directly by the Nationalist Government and is largely behind the military industries, iron and steel machinery, and mining machinery of the country.
NRC
The National Railway Corporation is operated by the Nationalist Government's Ministry of Railways as well as the Ministry of Communications and has been effective in nationalising formerly foreign-owned railways and is dedicated to the construction of new transportation networks throughout the country.
CETC
The CETC or China Electronics Technology Corporation is a corporation operated by the Nationalist Government's Ministry of Communications for the purposes of providing communications and civilian electronics for the purposes of the National Revolutionary Army.
Sinopec
Sinopec or China Petroleum & Chemical Corporation is a corporation organised by the Ministry of the Interior and manages the country's oil and petroleum reserves, while also encouraging oil and chemical extraction throughout the country.
Norinco
Norinco, which stands for the China North Industries Group Corporation Limited, is a corporation that is to manage the former industries of the Northern Chinese cliques such as the Fengtian and Zhili Clique. Organised by the Ministry of Commerce and the Interior, Norinco manages primarily military industries for the purposes of the National Revolutionary Army.
Faw Motors
With the help of European car manufacturers from the Union of Britain and the Commune of France, Faw Motors or First Automobile Works has broken ground as the first native Chinese state-owned automobile factory. It is dedicated to the production of modern automobiles for both civilian and military use.
CNAC
The China National Aviation Corporation was organised by order of the Executive Yuan under the leadership of both the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications. The CNAC was set up with help from both the Union of Britain and the Commune of France and at its conception faced resistance from military cliques in China which have their own individual air forces. As such the CNAC is established in order to oversee and nationalise all air traffic and air mail.
CANC
The Central Aircraft Manufacturing Company has been designed by the Nationalist Ministry of Air as a means to produce military and civilian grade aircraft for both the Republic of China Air Force and also for civilian transportation.
CAT
The Central Air Transport has been organised by the Ministry of Communications in order to facilitate air communication and transportation for both civilian and military uses throughout the country.
CSIC
The China Shipbuilding Industry Corporation is a state-owned ship-building industry organised by both the Ministry of Commerce and the Ministry of Navy in order to use former northern naval industries of the Fengtian and Zhili Clique for the purposes of building the new Nationalist navy.
CSSC
The China State Shipbuilding Corporation was created by orders of the Ministry of the Navy in order to facilitate the construction and production of warships, staffed with European designers and advisors as a way to modernise China's growing naval industry.
Sinotruk
Sinotruk or the China National Heavy Duty Truck Group Co., Ltd is state owned truck manufacturer designed from the basis of the former Jinan Automobile Works. It is known for producing China's own native trucks while also importing designs from foreign truck manufacturers for both military and civilian use.
The Kuomintang may have democratic and populist ideals, but it has a long way to go in terms of making those ideals into a reality. For the peasants and workers of China, plenty of dreamers have come and gone with their utopian promises and few have delivered. Battlefield victories may prove Kuomintang tenacity and perhaps may unify China under its banner, but if they wish to truly win over the hearts of the people, they must first save the hard-pressed commoners from their perennial strife.\n\nIt will take a long period of state building and careful policy implementation for the common people to see the Nationalist Government as legitimate, haughty declarations and fancy parades aside. In the meantime, plenty see the Kuomintang as hardly a step up from the warlord strongmen or as dangerous stooges of the faraway Syndicalist powers.

Legitimacy of the Party: §mA Democratic Consensus§!
In their quest to unite the nation, the Kuomintang has encountered dozens of other parties and factions along the way. Many were only looking out for their own self-interest, and almost all sought to oppose the national revolution. But Wang Jingwei had the insight and the diplomatic skill to bridge divisions in a tattered nation, building trust where there wasn't before. In an expanded party conference, Wang has allowed several allied warlords to join the government as advisors throughout the tutelage, taming the nation and co-opting popular ideals to China's betterment. In turn, he will ensure that these misguided parties will be tutored in the Three Principles, building a truly optimistic future.
Legitimacy of the Party: §RThe Premier's Guidance§!
The Kuomintang carried with it democratic and populist ideals but such ideals have fallen into doubt to the party's constant infighting. As the factions of the Party battled out their interpretations of Dr. Sun's teachings, the party's legitimacy and capability to rule became tarnished as a result. The fate of the Party remained unclear as Chairman Zeng Zhongming struggled to prop up a functioning government, full of some of the most radical socialists within the Kuomintang.\n\nOrder, reason, and logic has finally returned to China however under the guidance of Premier Chen Gongbo. While Chairman Zeng is the de facto ruler of China, those who can see behind the facade of bureaucracy and politics can see that it is indeed the Premier who holds all the cards in the country. Under Chen's instruction, the Party has stretched its control over the millions of people who are citizens of the country and under Chen's leadership shall China finally embark towards true socialism.
Legitimacy of the Party: §oTotally Reorganised Government§!
The Kuomintang carried with it democratic and populist ideals but such ideals have fallen into doubt thanks to the party's constant infighting. As the factions of the Party battled out their interpretations of Dr. Sun's teachings, the party's legitimacy and capability to rule became tarnished as a result. The fate of the Party remained unclear as Chairman Zeng Zhongming struggled to prop up a functioning government, full of some of the most radical socialists within the Kuomintang.\n\nThe counter-revolutionaries and the anti-RCA clique of Chen Bijun had attempted to dismantle everything that the late Chairman had built. In the chaos following the Third Congress, Chen Gongbo has risen to take up the Party's leadership as the rightful heir of Chairman Wang Jingwei and Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Now, with his control of the Party fully established, the reorganised Party can finally strive towards a totally socialist state and a platform of anti-imperialism. Led by RCA cadres, the Party shall lead the Peasants and Workers towards a glorious Red China and seek to show the world - that the East is now the bulwark of socialism.
Legitimacy of the Party:§o Total Abnegation of the Individual§!
The nation is supreme and sacred and it is the duty of the individual to pledge him or herself to the protection of national interests. We must forsake all earthly and individual pleasures and realise that the duty of every Chinese is to serve the State and to ensure that China will be strong forevermore.\n\nSeek to relinquish our freedoms and lives so that the Chinese country might finally be free of imperialism. Only then we will achieve freedom but it is a divine honour to serve and sacrifice for the nation. The Chinese citizen must perform his duties without speaking of rights, he will benefit when the nation becomes rich and strong. But the individual definitely cannot impose conditions on society before serving. Salvation for China today can be attained only through selflessly organising and obeying the Lingxiu and his right hand He Zhonghan. When the myriad masses are of one mind, their actions act as one body... truly there is no other way for us to attain the Three Principles.
Legitimacy of the Party: §oCult of the Lingxiu§!
The chaos of the aftermath of the Third Repatriated Congress and the Kuomintang Civil War led many to doubt the Party's leadership and see the Party as a weak political organ - unfit to lead the Chinese nation. However, in China's darkest hour, it was the Generalissimo who along with the glorious cadets and soldiers of the Whampoa Military Academy that have saved China from destruction by both foreign and domestic threats.\n\nIn order to preserve the revolution, the principle of obedience to the supreme leader must be followed. Hu Zongnan is the Kuomintang's only supreme leader and also China's only great leader; therefore members in the Party must absolutely support him, follow his orders only, and make his will their own. Obedience to the leader is unconditional. One must live and die with him, sincerely, unwaveringly - just as martyrs died for the late leader Sun Yat-sen. The youth of China, imbued with the follies of European syndicalism and liberalism have emphasised the individual, considering veneration of an idol as backward. But this is wrong, for the idol of the Party helps develop national culture and unifies the trust of the mass spirit. We cannot deny that the Party needs a Mussolini, it needs a Savinkov to guide it to glory - and in our Lingxiu Hu Zongnan, we will be able to achieve salvation for our nation!
Institute of Revolutionary Practice
It is by the success of the Party that we have managed to achieve what we have over the past years. Our work however is not done. Throughout this great country, there remains the need to train the party, the government, and the military to carry forward the revolutionary spirit of 1924 and to realise the success of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's vision for a free China.
Intellectual Opposition
For the last several years of the National Revolution, the Kuomintang has held a monopoly on political power and has ruled [CHI.GetNameDef] effectively as a Party-State. There are certainly those however, who agitate for more - who believe that the phase of tutelage must end and that the political area be opened up to fresh new discourse.
Popular Protests
The country has been riled up since the nation's recent dramatic events. The Kuomintang's claim to leadership is now once more within question as public outrage consumes the streets. Order must be restored quickly and with haste, before the protests turn into riots and riots into rebellion.

Legitimacy of the Party: §RTowards the Social Revolution§!
It is merely inevitable that upon the completion of the National Revolution against the bourgeoisie, the bullies, the landlords, and most of all the imperialists - that the Chinese Workers and Peasants shall be unified in one body. We herald the birth of a New China, one where no barriers shall infringe on the rights of every man and woman, and where can proudly proclaim their love and devotion to the Party and the revived Chinese nation.
Legitimacy of the Party: §STowards True Love§!
Real love cannot happen in this kind of world. It can happen only after the revolution, in a world of Great Harmony. When that time comes, there will be no distinction between rich and poor, no separation between beautiful and ugly, female and male. There will be common production, common benefits, equal knowledge, and education will be the same. Beauty will also be equal and people will all come together on the basis of love. Never again will there be a need for ulterior motives or some sort of calculated material motivation. This kind of love is what can be called true love.
Realising Minquan
Minquan, is the belief of administering the people's rights - that is the four rights of referendum, initiative, election, and recall. Obviously, the Chinese people are not yet ready to exercise these rights and can easily be exploited by local bullies and the gentry. As such, it is the Party's duty to teach them these rights and to help them realise minquan.\n§YThe effects of this idea is modified by your current $market_liberal_coloured$, $social_conservative_coloured$, and $authoritarian_democrat_coloured$ party popularity§!.
Nationalist Youth Organisations
Dr. Sun believed that it would also be the youths who must participate in the national revolution. The youth are the foundation of a revolutionary future and the spirit of the Chinese National Revolution as well as Chinese Nationalism must persist to the next generations if China is to be strong. For China's weaknesses lie in her lack of unity and if we disregard the youth - we will not prepare them for the revolutionary struggle in the future. Let us reach out to the youths via nationalist organisations and to encourage membership for both boys and girls, to learn and carry on Dr. Sun's Three Principles' of the People.
Local Democratic Elections
The Kuomintang adheres to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's beliefs that the rights of the people are the ability to exercise election, recall, referendum, and initiative. These rights must, however, be trained and taught by the Party, under the leadership of the Kuomintang and the creation of local governments with the help of the Party - can such a democracy flourish? It is the goal of the Party that by training the masses - that one day the people will fully be capable of democracy.
Local Communes
While unions existing in China may not seem realistic due to China's lack of industrialisation and lack of organised labour, the Kuomintang's should play a leading role in leading the National and Social Revolution by helping organise labourers and peasants into local associations so that they may be able to exercise their political rights and work towards achieving the people's livelihood.
The Third Stage of Revolution
The third-stage of the National Revolution is the final step in Dr. Sun's theory of a Three Stage Revolution. It calls for the end of political tutelage and the completion of the National Reconstruction. During this period, constitutional government is to be introduced, and the self-governing body of a district will enable the people directly to exercise their political rights. With the conclusion of national trials and the Second Northern Expedition, China may finally be able to realise the notion of the peoples' democracy.
Legitimacy of the Party: §lRealising the Dream of Sun Yat-sen§!
Dr. Sun Yat-sen called for a revolution for all people, quanmin geming - and that the National Revolution was for all people in China not just the peasants and workers. Long has our party been separated by ideals such as class struggle but with the help of Sun Fo's Reconstruction Faction, it is not a Reorganisation but rather a Reconstruction of the Party that we seek. With the completion of the Second Northern Expedition and the War of Resistance, China has finally thrown off the chains of warlordism and imperialism. Forward, we march towards a bright new White dawn of democracy and civil rights - let us finally realise the dream of dear late leader, and seek to inspire the rest of the East to follow our example.
Foreign Development Funding
Ever since the hosting of the Afro-Asian Conference in Nanjing, there has been a greater impetus to break the old imperialist, capitalist system. Thanks to some generous backing from socialist powers, we have received industrial and financial aid meant to help us drift away from the old colonial system. With any luck, this will mark the first steps in building a new post-colonial order.
Champion of the Developing World
China has emerged from the ashes of civil war and revolution as a great Dragon, a power to behold even for the mightiest of nations. But like the short-sighted imperialists of old, the Republic has sought to expand its influence not merely with martial prowess but also leveraging its burgeoning economic might. It will be many decades before China will be able to fully compete with European powers, but the Chinese have sought to claim the mantle of Champion of developing socialist states across the Pacific and beyond.
MMIC-NRA Cooperation
The Internationale Military Mission in China and the National Revolutionary Army have a long standing tradition and history of working together since the NRA's return to the Chinese country following nearly a decade of exile. With the help of the military advisors from the Internationale, the National Revolutionary Army has been reorganised along modern military lines and is now truly a power to reckon with. The MMIC has now approached us to renew this cooperation and to begin a new training programme in the hopes of working together with our armed forces in preparation for future conflict.
Exiles from the Third Internationale
The Mission Militaire Internationale en Chine was deployed to China by the Third Internationale following the League War - ensuring a close period of cooperation between the nations of the Third Internationale and Nanjing's revolutionary government. While certainly controversial with factional disagreements with the Chinese Kuomintang in regards to the extent of Internationale involvement (with hostile critics claiming that the revolution was being increasingly led by Paris and London), the MMIC's role in creating a modern revolutionary army was undeniably instrumental to the success of the national revolution.\n\nNow with the revolution crushed in both Paris and London, thousands of exiles from the Third Internationale have arrived in China. Now seen as one of the last beacons of socialist hope, these spirited officers have pledged their service to the continuation of the revolution and their goal of returning home to their former countries.
Loyalist Infighting
Wang Jingwei's followers may have been united together against the Provisional Action Committee and their reactionary allies but knives are being sharpened as the factionalism between Wang's own supporters are beginning to show. The RCA finds itself torn between its Radical and Moderate factions and the Residence Faction seeks to restrain and control the RCA, so that only it alone has the attention of the Chairman.
Mass Disillusionment
Can Wang Jingwei really save China from years of strife and instability? The events of the recent Third Congress have shown that the stability promised by the Chairman is in doubt with many doubting whether or not the defeat of the Provisional Action Committee will actually bring democracy and stability to China. Unless matters are taken to address the ongoing disillusionment throughout the cities and streets, China continues to lie anxious...
Demoralised Army
The National Revolutionary Army has effectively been purged following the full consolidation of the Chairman. Nervous and anxious about potentially being purged next, members of NRA who are opposed to Wang have kept themselves silent. The army lies bitterly demoralised and is in an incompetent state, the Chairman must take steps to recover and consolidate control of the NRA, in order to restore it to a functional form.
Technocratic Administration
The bloated bureaucracy of the Kuomintang has been thoroughly rid of its demagogues and ideologues and the Party can now focus on truly being effective and passing its much needed reforms. Furthermore, we will invite those with foreign training to help grow and reform our government.

Chinese Industrial Volunteers
While the Chairman is reluctant to bring us into yet another conflict after years of war and conflict have destabilised the Chinese country - we do owe our friends in the Third Internationale our thanks for taking care of us over the years of exile. We will dispatch thousands of Chinese labourers and volunteers to help develop their nations so that they too may feel that our debt to them is slowly being paid off.
Invite Foreign Investors
While the Republic of China is finally at long last rising back to its feet, let us encourage Western and foreign investors from the socialist nations of the world to help aid and fund the development of our country. As we are years behind the West, it is important that we hire Western experts so that they may trach us their secrets of success and help us resist economic imperialism.
Unfulfilled Promises
The Kuomintang received a plethora of support from domestic and foreign elements due to their promises of democracy and improving the welfare of the oppressed peoples. However, the recent events of the Kuomintang Civil War have not given the masses the stability they had expected. The Party's promises are falling on deaf ears and unless something is done soon, the influence of the Party will only continue to weaken.
Devastated Nation
With great optimism, our economic reforms helped restore faith in our national economy and helped rebuild the country after decades of warlordism. It was this industry that allowed China the capabilities of resisting the Japanese imperialists during the War of Resistance and it is with this hope that we believed that our economy would only move forward.\n\nThe Kuomintang Civil War has interrupted all pretences of rapid economic and industrial growth as the devastation caused by the war has severely damaged the national economy. It will take time to rebuild and heal the wounds of civil war which shall hopefully restore hope in our capabilities of leading the Chinese Republic.
Disloyal Army
The National Revolutionary Army while employed by the Party and effectively an instrument of the National Revolution, has long enjoyed its autonomy in administrative and operational decisions. While loyalty to the Party is stressed within the Army, Chen Gongbo's paranoia and the chaos of the Kuomintang Civil War has alienated many within the Army to the ideals of the Party. While the Army was once staffed with many Whampoa Military Academy Revolutionary Classmates Association (WMARCA) members, the civil war has effectively expelled much of the former PAC leadership. As a result there are rumours of revolt and dissatisfaction within the army ranks... just rumours of course, the Army wouldn't dare try anything against the Party... or would they?
Expel the Landlords
The landlord is the greatest example of injustice in our semi-feudal society as the peasants are forced to devote their lives and labour to the landlords who offer them nothing in return. For the peasants must toil and work to survive while the landlords are able to live like capitalists, comfortably off their harsh labour. We shall declare an open war against all landowners with large properties and expel them so that their land can be distributed to the people.
Ongoing Resistance
We may have won the war but we have yet to win the peace. Throughout the country, organised resistance is growing against our leadership of the Party. If we are to maintain our legitimacy as the true leaders of the National Revolution, then we must seek to do something at once and eradicate domestic terrorism once and for all.
The Rump Government
What is left of the Kuomintang's bureaucratic democracy has fallen into a shell of its former self following the conclusion of the Kuomintang Civil War and the chaos of the Third Repatriated Congress. Sun Fo leads a weak coalition of his few remaining supporters but everyone knows that the Reconstruction Faction no longer holds much influence within the Party. Shattered Political Order
The liberation (or some may say conquest) of China by syndicalist powers has offered the chance for the Chinese people to cast off the chains of imperialism, warlordism, and capitalism - but for now leaves the nation in a state of almost perpetual political disarray. Many liberals and reactionaries actively work to undermine the new government, and even within the Chinese left the many in the sidelined Kuomintang establishment refuse to work with what they see as a foreign-imposed revisionist socialism. Military Affairs Commission
Following Chen Jiongming's attempt to usurp the Kuomintang in Guangdong with the Eastern Expeditions, the National Revolutionary Army created the Military Affairs Commission (MAC) to oversee and act as the highest military decision making body under the Central Executive Committee. Made up of important military and political officials, the MAC follows a longer tradition of centralised war councils and in many ways has considerable power on its own right. With the return of the NRA as a formidable military force in China - the Military Affairs Commission has been officially reinstated in order to better command and organise the army of the national revolution.

Zhongyang Teke
The Special Service section of the Central Committee (nicknamed the Zhongyang Teke), is the name of the intelligence agency led by General Zhou Enlai and his fellow compatriots in the Political Department. With high connections within the Party, the Shanghai Underworld, and the labour unions of the Legation Cities - the Teke is tasked with the suppression of internal dissent, opposition, counter-intelligence, and espionage in order to maintain the Party's line.
Bureau of Investigation and Statistics of the Military Affairs Commission
Bureau of Investigation and Statistics of the Military Affairs Commission (BIS) is the name of the intelligence agency headed by the shadowy Dai Chunfeng and his \
Ministry of State Security
Formed as a compromise between the competing Zhongyang Teke and the National Bureau of Investigation and Statistics, the Ministry of State Security was created by order of the Central Committee in order to administer the party's line in matters of internal security, while also establishing a network of counter-intelligence and espionage to monitor and defend the national revolution from enemies within and outside.
Disorderly NRA
Despite resounding successes on the battlefield and the bravery the soldiers of the National Revolutionary Army showed during the Second Northern Expedition, the NRA has grown severely bloated as a result of incorporating thousands of defectors, volunteers, and the capturing of enemy stockpiles. At the same time, paradoxically, many of the army's elite starting units have grown depleted as the expedition went on, some existing effectively only on paper. Their reinforcements have been either delayed or redirected as logistics snarled going northwards.\n\nThe pervasive, nearly systematic, rot that has spread across the army has become impossible to excise. If we are to save it from becoming a shambling mass of men, the only realistic solution left is to temporarily demobilise entire army corps wholescale and rebuild anew division by division. This is a tall order and expected to face significant resistance, especially since warlord units will face the brunt of disbandment orders.
Demobilising NRA
Some progress has been made in rebuilding the NRA, though problems continue. Many local commanders have resisted our orders to disband, fearing that our efforts will come primarily at the expense of their power. Others fear demobilisation will leave their sectors unguarded, or hesitate to split apart units that have years of camaraderie.\n\nStill, brigade by brigade and regiment by regiment our divisions are slowly being reconstituted once more into fighting units. As the frontline solidifies somewhat, a more steady logistical train has been established, thus alleviating some pressing concerns about the state of our military. Time is of the essence however, it is only a matter of time before the NRA is once more called to protect and defend China.
Disorganised NRA
The sweeping successes of the National Revolutionary Army during the Northern Expedition hid a growing problem within its ranks: that of outrunning its logistical tail and becoming over-bloated like the armies of the warlords. After thorough discussion and realising there was no other options, the Military Affairs Commission ordered a thorough demobilisation.\n\nIt was a painful process but it seems that the worst of it is behind us now. Most of our best divisions are fully restored, and those we have raised or acquired along the way have been largely integrated into our ranks. There remain many command and control issues at a corps and army level, though this can be chalked up to growing pains as our freshly build army balloons in size. They must remain vigilant however - this vanguard of the revolution has considerable ground to make up as we continue onwards to national liberation.
The Disbandment Conference
Faced with a bloated, severely overextended army at the end of the Northern Expedition, the Military Affairs commission has ordered a drastic solution: the manually disbanding of entire divisions and corps in order to rebuild them unit by unit.\n\nAfter a major conference to address the issue, it became clear that not every unit disbanded would eventually be reformed: to save costs and to secure the primacy of the National Revolutionary Army, various provincial divisions have been mandated to outright demobilise, in the aims of eventual integration.
Birthplace of the Second Revolution

Standardised Army Organisation
At the National Disbandment Conference, the National Revolutionary Army agreed to standardise the military composition of divisions into two distinctive types. These measures are undertaken in order to promote unity within the large NRA as well as to reduce army bloat. It is our hope that by these reforms, we will be able to modernise our military forces quickly.

Workplace Democracy

The Two-Stage Revolution
Members of the Chinese Syndicalist Party's Orthodox Faction believe that the Chinese Revolution is a two-stage revolution. That is that while the great majority of the Chinese peasantry can be drawn into the national revolution, it will be the intellectuals and petite bourgeoisie who can play a special role in uniting all other classes including merchants, workers, and peasants. At this time in history, the Chinese peasants and workers are too weak to lead the revolution, only when the development of capitalism reaches certain levels can the syndicalists begin to talk about a proletarian revolution.

Revitalised Economy
Slowly but surely, our efforts are bearing fruit. Once ravaged by the plight of war, the provinces of the former League of Eight Provinces are finally on their way to recovery. No longer bound to the mountains of Fujian, we can seek to fully utilise the land and its resources for the purposes and success of the National Revolution.
Intensify Reconstruction Efforts
We will seek to intensify our reconstruction efforts of the former League of Eight Provinces. Let us show that the Kuomintang is here to free China and that we seek to uplift the lives of the workers and peasants of this country.
Empowering Urban Workers
The Kuomintang has concentrated much of their recent energies into a rush of enthusiasm for urban development. This includes programmes to retrain and employ workers, organising industrial leadership, and creating new supply chain networks as well as other programmes for those injured at work or retired. Furthermore, money has been given for cleaning up wartime damages, improving the housing situation in various slums, and basic social services. Although small in scope, and mostly concentrated in the capital, the Kuomintang effort is a concrete step towards their idealistic promises for the future.
Empowering Rural Peasants
The Kuomintang has concentrated much of their recent energies into helping the downtrodden peasants, who have faced major disruptions due to the warlord era fighting. With the money they have, efforts have been made to help partially mechanise farming, protect crops from pests, and build more water control methods to help reduce the uncertainty of harvest. There is a long way to go across the board, but these efforts signify the Kuomintang's continued commitment to their rural base.
Empowering the People
The Kuomintang has distributed their energies across their major pillars of support: the peasants, workers, and the intellectuals that back their movement. In the cities, some basic assistance has been given to urban programmes related to reopening factories and retraining workers. In the fields, projects have gone underway to give the farmers loans and assistance in recovering their harvest. And in the universities, museums, and conservatories, idealistic intellectuals have been given artistic and science grants with the intention of help creating new culture and life to a battered nation.
Focusing on State-building
The Kuomintang government has worked to stabilise itself by streamlining its finances and ensuring steady pay-checks for its growing bureaucracy. Although not the most flashy or creative use of its assets, such a project is ambitious nonetheless - creating a modern socialist state from the ashes of decades of warlordism. It won't be easy, but as a new leviathan arises across the land, hope emerges that there may be a government to last.
Focusing on Industrialisation
The Kuomintang government has worked to build up an industrial power-base in their heartland, building factories, lay tracks, paving roads, and clearing out slums in their quest to out-produce their enemies. Although the infusion of wealth into this programme has been useful, further sacrifices are to be expected on the long road to a modern China.
Focusing on Army Modernisation
The Kuomintang government has worked to modernise their military by purchasing foreign designs and licenses and distributing grants for local inventors who are able to create feasible improvements in nearly all fields of military development. This has spurred patriotic faculty, researchers, engineers, and even students to race to create better grenades, rifles, and even artillery designs for the salvation of their country.
Over one century of foreign and domestic humiliation has placed China as one of the world's most backwards economies with many regarding China as merely a third-rate nation lagging behind in technology and modernity. As our hold of the Chinese country now grows to encompass the former capital of Beijing, we have emerged as an indisputable national unifier and as such, we must prepare to seek to implement the late Dr. Sun's National Reconstruction Commission.\n\nThe road to economic recovery will not be easy and it will not be quick. Return of the Second NRA
Once believed to be the army capable of unifying China, the National Revolutionary Army split apart during the fallout of the Northern Expedition. After nearly a decade of fighting the guerrilla war in the MinGan Zone, the NRA has returned with its full strength - hoping to carry out one last uprising for salvation.
Fortify the MinGan Zone
For years, we have familiarised ourselves with the mountains and forests of the Jiangxi and Fujian region - turning our exile into the bulwark of a new national revolution. Petition the Internationale for Aid
Since our party's founder Dr. Sun Yat-sen sought the Internationale for aid and recognition in organising the reorganisation of the Kuomintang in 1924, we have maintained cordial ties with our revolutionary comrades in the Internationale. The Hundred Workshops Programme

Our Comrades Overseas
While most members of the Kuomintang fled for exile in China or in Europe, there were also those who followed Sun Fo and other centrists - into exile in Hawaii and Southeast Asia. Long disconnected from the KMT, with news of our revolution spreading - they have offered their vocal and financial support for our new uprising.
Rally the Mass Movement
As instructed by our late founder, the Kuomintang is to lead the oppressed classes of China to break their chains and to work together in order to resist the imperialists and their warlord lackeys. Enforce Discipline
As the NRA finds itself once more in open conflict, we must ensure that our comrades serving in the militias are disciplined and adequately follow the rules of civility. For we must ensure that the Kuomintang's NRA earns a reputation as a formidable fighting force and one capable of discipline and respect.
Wage Protracted War
Outnumbered and outgunned, for years the NRA that has resided in Fujian has learned that fights can be won by unconventional means. Rally the Militias!
Since the widow of our late founder, Song Qingling established the MinGan Insurgency - the leading officers and generals of the NRA in China have been tasked in training and educating the peasants to organise themselves into revolutionary militias. If the Chinese people are to transition to a state of democracy, then we must encourage the militias to defend this freedom.
Encourage our Revolutionary Sisters
Taking the example of the great revolutionary Song Qingling, thousands of women serve in the MinGan Insurgent Zone as teachers, nurses, writers, and volunteers - all eager to not only win freedom for China but also to achieve equality for all sexes in the ensuring revolution. Let us encourage the creation of a woman's volunteer unit to aid in our struggle.
All for the Nation
As the situation looks increasingly grim on the front-lines, remember comrades of our valiant struggles such as the Battle at Mianhu, where the high-spirited yet outnumbered Whampoa students managed to defeat a much larger force led by Chen Jiongming. In those same ideals of self-sacrifice, honour, and bravery, let us inspire the NRA to carry on the same Whampoa spirit one last time.
Host the First Repatriated Congress
After nearly a decade in exile, the Chinese Kuomintang has surpassed all odds and has once more established a formidable presence in the chaotic political situation of China. With the success of the NRA in the League War, calls have been sent out throughout the Chinese country - to rally support for the Kuomintang's First Repatriated Congress as a reunited and revived political force.
Restore the Political Department
The secret ingredient to the National Revolutionary Army's total dedication to the Kuomintang cause is their thorough political education conducted by party representatives in the Political Department. This created an ideological backbone in each Whampoa cadet that allowed the NRA to go toe-to-toe with much larger warlord armies - only German intervention could save them. It is high time we revive this department.
Deal with the Warlords
Warlordism is a blight on the Chinese nation, an oppressive institution that threatens not only national unity but prosperity. As we find our footing, having driven out the local warlords in the League, we must not forget the millions of others living under the boots of petty tyrants. It is too early to challenge our rivals for national leadership, but in the mean time we shall oust militarists as opportunities arise.
Eyes in the Dark
Real strategy requires cunning, and for all the bright coloured banners and flowery language that accompanies liberation, in the shadows lies plenty of opportunities for skullduggery. If we are to stay one step ahead of opponents, we need to coordinate our intelligence efforts, and that means creating a formal espionage apparatus. Fittingly, there will be plenty of intrigue involved in deciding on an agency.
Revive the Military Affairs Commission
An army without leadership is a mob, and as the National Revolutionary Army spreads its wings it needs now more than ever capable men at the helm. Modern military organisation means that no one person could ever lead a campaign alone: a council of staff, experts, and commanders are needed. The army however is haunted by ghosts of its past, as it resolves who ought to sit on the revived MAC.
Complete the Revolutionary Mission
Even as Dr. Sun approached the end of his life, he dreamed that the party would one day march north from its bases in Guangzhou to liberate the nation - toppling the failed Beiyang government. Although he knew it was unlikely he'd see the day (finally succumbing to cancer in Beijing during negotiations), with our forces gathered we will finally meet him there in that city. Once again, we march for the freedom of the nation, and for the Eternal Premier's sake we will not fail!
Provisional Legislative Yuan
The concept of the Legislative Yuan owes itself to the late Dr. Sun's Three Principles of the People that proposed a separation of power into five branches, with the Yuan being the law making organ when the Assembly is not in session. Since our position is still precarious however, let us seek to legitimise the Party's rule by establishing a provisional yuan for the revolutionary government.
Establish the National Bureaucracy
While our party's late founder Dr. Sun envisioned that there would be a necessary stage of the party-state and tutelage, we must undertake efforts to legitimise our control of the former League. Until the country is reunified, we will have to hold off on drafting a constitution. Nonetheless, an organic law shall be passed to govern in a constitution's stead, ushering in the return of a formal Executive Yuan.
Tender to the Masses
As part of the Kuomintang's commitment to the mass movement, the Party is to be the vanguard to represent the oppressed workers and peasants of China from the chains of their local bullies, the corrupt bourgeois gentry, and the imperialists. If we are to succeed in bringing the revolution to China, then we must teach the true people of China to rise up and realise their revolutionary potential.
Promote Revolutionary Culture
Since the Xinhai Revolution of 1911, new thinkers and ideas have emerged into the Chinese political and literary scene as those in our country have sought to find connections with Chinese values and Western ideals. In order to strengthen the revolutionary cause, we will inspire the creation of such a revolutionary culture - to support and direct the people's art to support the cause of our revolution.
The Liberation of the Chinese Woman
As our experiences in the MinGan Zone showed, the national revolution is not just the struggle of the Chinese people against the imperialists, but it is also a social revolution, a revolution to uproot centuries of oppression and to bring forth a new era of equality. As such, we will encourage our country's women to take part in the revolution and fight for a new world for themselves.
Formulate Land Distribution
While certainly a controversial and hotly debated issue between the multiple factions within the Kuomintang, the time has come to discuss the preliminary acts of a comprehensive land reform in order to strengthen the mass movement and to end feudal practices once and for all. As part of the revolutionary direction, we shall seek to address the long-standing issue of land reform in China.
Power to the United Front
As part of our promise to the Third Internationale in exchange for arms, supplies, and recognition from the socialist nations of the West; we are to undertake the Chinese National Revolution with the aid of the League of Chinese Syndicalists. Together, let us work together in a new united front to free our nation from imperialism once and for all.
Intensify Reconstruction Efforts
As one of China's most developed regions, the former League of Eight Provinces still lies ravaged by the recent liberation by the National Revolutionary Army. If we are to continue the revolution and earn the support of the masses, then we must seek to rapidly intensify our reconstruction efforts of eastern China in order to build a suitable base for the National Revolutionary Government.
Nationalise the Railways
Long has the Chinese worker been forced to toil, sweat, and bleed for the dark and steaming mines and railways of the imperialist colonisers who have exploited China's resources and wealth for their own. With the success of the National Revolution in Eastern China, we shall seek to take over all foreign railway industries and tracks in order to utilise their strength for the Chinese nation.
Redistribute Warlord Assets
Too long have the masses in China been oppressed by the corrupt and brutal warlords that have divided our great country. With our recent victory over several of these warlords, we now have access to their assets and property, which we may see fit to return to the people or to utilise them for the sake and purposes of the national revolution.
The Ministry of Communications
Propaganda can be disseminated in various ways from pamphlets and newspapers, but also through modern methods such as broadcasting and the radio. By direct order of the Central Committee, we will create the Ministry of Communications to accomplish this task of national broadcasting. Not only must we win the wars of unification but we must also win the hearts and minds of the people.
Develop the MinGan Region
The MinGan Insurgent Zone was for a while, the last bastion of the nationalist revolution in China. While we certainly applaud the efforts of Song Qingling's populist government in the region, with our access to greater resources - we now have the opportunity to further develop this important region and improve our support with the people of Jiangxi and Fujian.
Revive Eastern China
Weeks of battle and disorder has led to chaos and destruction along the eastern provinces of China in places such as Jiangsu and Anhui. While the Kuomintang has been at work in reorganising local governments and repairing infrastructure, let us intensify reconstruction efforts in these provinces in order to strengthen support and to build up our revolutionary base government.
Bulwark of the National Revolution
At last, we have returned. Nanjing - the city of the Ming emperors and the former presidential capital of our late beloved Dr. Sun Yat-sen, has finally been liberated by the National Revolutionary Army. It is here in Nanjing where the flame of revolution continues to burn unbothered, where the flag of the Blue Sky, White Sun, and Wholly Red Earth shall guide the great rays of the national revolution!
Reinforce the Foreign Ministry
In order to achieve international recognition with not just the nations of the world but also of the Chinese expatriate diaspora, we will re-establish the former foreign ministry of the Party to propagate our ideals and our mission to the world. Furthermore, let us reach out to the oppressed peoples of Asia to look to our revolution as inspiration for carrying out their own national liberation.
Our Shanghai Connections
While seen as the high water mark of Western imperialism in China, Shanghai is home to thousands of workers and gangsters who are sympathetic to our pursuit of the national revolution - it was also the city in which many in the Party fled to after the failure of the Northern Expedition. With our position on the Chinese eastern seaboard secured, let us re-establish these connections in the Pearl of the East.
Reopen the Whampoa Military Academy
In 1924, in accordance with the ideals of Sun Yat-sen, the Whampoa Military Academy was created to house China's next generation of officers and generals to partake in the national revolution. With the return of the Kuomintang in China once more, the Central Committee has unanimously agreed to authorise the re-establishment of the military academy in preparation for national unification.
Legacy of the MinGan Insurgency
As the NRA shifts from unconventional warfare to conventional warfare, our high command has agreed to maintain the tactics and strategies mastered during the MinGan insurgency. This method of war focuses on rapid movements throughout rough terrain, fighting defensively when it is called for, waging a protracted war, and seeking out encirclements in order to annihilate larger enemy forces.
Embrace Encirclement Tactics
As we will often find ourselves outnumbered, let us seek to disrupt enemy communications through harassment, ambush, and sabotage with preliminary attacks before having our soldiers manoeuvre sneakily between enemy forces, and then dealing fatal blows at weak points in enemy lines. Once we have surrounded the enemy, we will continue to press our attacks to fully annihilate them until they have no escape.
Masters of the Land
Those who have served in the Jiangxi-Fujian Insurgency or had partaken in the earlier First Northern Expedition have accumulated years of practical military experience in the Chinese countryside. Each officer is thoroughly familiar with the people of his home town, the seasonal patterns of his home province, and the terrain of whom he had grown up with. With this mastery of the land comes invaluable experience.
Revolutionary Arms
In the hills of Fujian where the flames of revolution continued to burn, the National Revolutionary Army was forced to either hope that arms shipments from the Internationale would reach the Fujian government safely or instead turned to locally producing copies of existing Western or Chinese firearms. Let us continue that tradition by encouraging the workers of the land to produce arms for the revolutionary army.
Strike Quick, Strike Fast
In Western military theory,initiative is often a kinetic force directly based on offensive action but within the NRA, initiative is a potential force - it is a freedom of action, the ability of an army to go where its commander wishes it to go. The idea of retreat follows this concept naturally, by withdrawing tactically from engagement - we are able to retain movement in the face of a stronger attack.
The People's War
We wage a revolution not purely for the sake of the national revolution against imperialism but also a revolution for the oppressed peoples of China - long bound to their feudal chains. Let us encourage the people to rise up with us, as our soldiers march proudly through the liberated areas - we will encourage those who will want to eat and be free, to join us in our glorious cause.
Adopt Unconventional Means
While armies in China are used to fighting in conventional manners, our forces have long earned their expertise in the guerrilla zone by taking advantage of much larger enemy forces with harassment, ambush, and sabotage. The farther the enemy penetrates into our base area, the longer and more vulnerable his communications and supply lines become - the easier we are able to strike him where he can't see.
Army of the Revolution
The effectiveness of a modern military command structure does not depend only on the capabilities of its individual members, it also depends on their cohesion to the greater mission ahead. The officers and generals of the National Revolutionary Army are dedicated men to the Kuomintang and to the shared belief that they fight for their nation's salvation and freedom.
Renovate the Fujianese Naval Academies
Fujian is home to many sailors and across the Five Provinces many maritime institutions have been established over the years. The realities of the warlord era meant that naval development has seen the short end of the stick when it comes to military priorities: the League did the bare minimum to patrol their coasts. Now that we are masters of much of China's eastern seaboard, it is our duty to keep it safe.
Encourage Political Commissars
\
Dare to Die Corps
The tradition of heroic martyrdom dates back to the years before the Xinhai Revolution, when revolutionary martyrs charged forward into battle without a care for their life but filled with devotion to their country. Now that we find ourselves in pursuit of the revolutionary mission, we must encourage those within our forces to be prepared to give the ultimate sacrifice necessary.
Renovate the Jinling Arsenal
The Jinling Arsenal built by the Qing Dynasty in 1865 was one of China's first modern arsenals - designed to help design and produce ordinance and other more heavier weaponry. Left behind to waste by the Zhili warlords and abandoned during the chaotic fighting of the League War, let us seek to renovate the former arsenal and turn it into the armoury of the revolution.
Inherit our Comrades' Arms
Years of exile and reliance on the Third Internationale has led us to become familiarised with the weaponry of our European socialist friends. Their arsenals contain many now outdated pieces such as the French 75 mm, that nonetheless can be repurposed for military use in China. Their weapons that once helped them win their own revolutions at home, will now serve to aid our revolution.
Look to the West
In the same way that the Kuomintang is bringing progress to the nation, the National Revolutionary Army must be a vanguard for Chinese military development. Many officers have studied extensively in modern European military academies across the last decade, and are ready to apply those lessons to build a new National Revolutionary Army with the latest in doctrine and technology.
Encourage Widespread Radio Use
A major innovation used during the Great War in Europe was the radio, which tremendously expanded military communication as well as enhanced command and control in the battlefield. The use of radios is still in its infancy in China, but with some effort we can quickly augment our forces with this new technology - critical for coordinated, concentrated strikes in vulnerable enemy positions.
Create the Supply Corps
\
Mechanised Units
Some pragmatic compromises have to be made, even as we begin sweeping changes to our military structure. Du Yuming is a long-time WMARCA commander but has expressed willingness to lead in the creation of a mechanised force - proof that politics does not have to get in the way of professionalism. A mobile strike force for our revolutionary army will give us a key advantage over our warlord rivals.
Force Concentration
If we are to avoid stalemates and the grinding sort of conflict that we can ill afford, we must take inspiration from the lessons learned in the trenches of the last major war. After careful scouting and planning, weak points in enemy lines must be assailed in one great, focused attack using modern combined arms. The widening breach will allow for breakthroughs to win us the day.
Tighten Army Centralisation
In the insurgency period, command and control was an utter mess - left to the poorly coordinate initiative of various militia commanders. This might have worked in evading League patrols, where competent generals were often purged and the elite German trained units held in Nanjing to keep Sun Chuanfang in power, but a real staff officer system must be created if we are fight against determined foes.
Study European Air Tactics
A critical force multiplier that has been increasingly refined in Europe is the development of modern air arms. Initially used as a means of reconnaissance, its applications have multiplied across the last few decades - even warlords have been buying planes. André Malraux has gathered foreign volunteer pilots to serve us as we train Chinese ground crews, but one day we will claim the skies for our own.
The Modern NRA
The Modern NRA is one built along European lines, one that integrates artillery, armour, and aircraft with advanced communications and dedicated logistics. It is the vanguard of a new China, a revolutionary force that was meant to be since Whampoa first opened. It is the legacy of countless martyrs, whose blood will ensure that China will soon be able to stand toe to toe with European imperialists!
The Northern Expedition Avenged!
It has finally been done. The revolutionary mission passed down to us from Dr. Sun and Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek has finally been achieved, this time without the intervention of [GER.GetNameDef]. With the national revolution secured in both Nanjing and Beijing, the time has come for the rest of China to finally come together under the leadership of the KMT. Zhonghua Minguo Wansui!
A New Day in Beiping
Following the reconquest of Beijing from the perfidious warlords and the so-called \
Host the Second Repatriated Congress
The Chinese Nationalist Party has succeeded where so many have failed and as such, it is appropriate once more to convene a grand congress of leftists, revolutionaries, patriots, and other like-minded individuals to draft and plan out the next phase of the Chinese Revolution. Topics of discussion will range from economic reform to dealing with the ever-present threat of [JAP.GetNameDef].
Embrace Autarky
To many in the Kuomintang, the roots of China's woes lie in her unfortunate economic dependence on the imperialist world - which seeks to do nothing more than to take advantage of her natural resources and wealth. With the leadership of the Party, we will embrace the notion and idea of economic self-sufficiency, however we will also promote the growth of national capitalism in select coastal regions to help develop our economy.
National Reconstruction Commission
The National Reconstruction Commission was the idea of the late Dr. Sun to help rebuild China's economy after years of foreign humiliation. We will seek to end the era of being a semi-feudal and semi-colonial state by embarking on a rapid and vast programme of modernisation, bringing China from the developing world to one that can hopefully rival the West.
Create the NEC
In order to better coordinate the National Reconstruction Commission, a committee known as the National Economic Council has been set up to manage the country's new autarkic policies as well as to promote the rapid industrialisation and extraction of our natural resources. Through careful and bureaucratic centralised economic planning, we will be able to bring about the administrative and economic unification of our country.
Develop the Heavy Industry Sector
Despite the industrial port cities, industrialisation in China is still lacking compared to the rest of the world. While most of our initial industrial reforms were centred around the development of light and civilian industries, we will expand our industrial efforts by promoting the creation of larger industrial projects for both civilian and military use.
Secure Foreign Recognition
As few would dispute our legitimacy at this point with our capture of Beijing, it is imperative that we reach out to the Western nations especially our friends in the Third Internationale to receive recognition as the sole Republic of China. While we are still waging an offensive to win the hearts and minds of the Chinese people, we must also seek to establish our international reputation.
Entrenching Dangguo
Following the collapse of the NRA and the First Northern Expedition, few dared to dream that the flag of the White Sun, Blue Sky, and Wholly Red Earth would fly over Beijing. Despite the completion of the Second Northern Expedition, there are still those who threaten the success of the revolution. As we end the military phase of the revolution, we must work together in this next phase of political tutelage to safeguard our goals.
The Fate of Our Fellow Republicans
With the success of the Second Northern Expedition, the Kuomintang has emerged from a shattered revolutionary movement back into the situation of national contender-ship. As the Nationalist Party now holds both the Northern and Southern Capital, let us reach out to fellow non-Party aligned republicans and determine their stance of support towards the National Revolution.
Preparing for the Long War
It will not come easy. The enemy will push into our cities, ravage our coastline, and torment our long-divided nation. At times, we will be forced to fall back - perhaps even towards the interior of the country - but we will never surrender our civilisation away. The war will be long, but our determination to win shall last even longer - we will accept nothing less than absolute victory.
The Third Repatriated Congress
With the conclusion of the War of Resistance and the unification of Manchuria back into China, the Kuomintang is finally able to proclaim itself as the true Republic of China. As the Republican dream is fully revived once more, the Party plans to host its third national congress imminently, but fractures within the Party may lead to dramatic consequences for the Chinese nation...
In Pursuit of the People's Welfare
Minsheng is belief in ensuring that the Chinese people have access to equal opportunities and livelihoods. The late founding father of the Party, Dr. Sun, believed that livelihood must be expanded into the areas of clothing, food, housing, and mobility. Under the Nationalist Government, we shall take steps to ensure our society draws closer to this principle.
Establish the National Health Administration
Inspired by advances in European healthcare, the National Health Administration (NHA) is an organisation established by the Party's Ministry of Health. Inspired by Dr. Sun's belief that a physically weak nation cannot survive in the competitive world, the NHA will accomplish this by creating vaccination and sanitation programmes, local health clinics, and rural mobile health centres.
Academia Sinica
The Academia Sinica was created after the Second Repatriated Congress of the Kuomintang following the passage of the Organic Law of the Academia Sinica - a project proposed by the World Society. The Academy is directly under the National Government and shall offer classes in a multitude of subjects from geology to new, modern Western ideas such as psychology.
Institute of Revolutionary Practice
As our territory grows significantly larger in size, from the former insurgency region of the MinGan Zone and then to the National Revolutionary Government, we must remind comrades of the true revolutionary nature of their mission. Furthermore, we must help the people realise their revolutionary consciousness - to turn them into a revolutionary vanguard.
The Disbandment Conference
Organised by the main military leaders of the National Revolutionary Army, a National Disbandment Commission is hereby established to deal with the NRA's bloated size and problems after the Second Northern Expedition. The posts of commander in chief, field commanders, and other wartime tactical roles are to be abolished and efforts initiated to disband all superfluous troops.
Fate of the Beiyang Army
While the Beiyang and other warlord regimes were merely institutions of corruption and outlets for foreign imperialism to exploit the Chinese people, there are certainly those officers and generals who are progressive enough that they are willing to offer their services to the National Revolutionary Army. As a way to handle reconstruction faster, let us provide them with commissions so that they may now serve the Party.
Standardise Army Organisation
The National Revolutionary Army, by order of the National DIsbandment Commission, is hereby authorised to adopt two forms of division types to standardise military organisation. With the conclusion of both the guerrilla phase of revolution and the Second Northern Expedition, the NRA is now to transition from the People's Army to one that is capable of bringing the national revolution to Asia.
Repossess National Arsenals
As our forces have liberated China with the fervour of unification, we have seized multiple abandoned arms factories and arsenals left behind by their provincial warlords - many of whom have built up arms-production facilities of their own over the years. Let us utilise these arsenals and upgrade them so that they may serve the needs of the Party and nation, rather than another power-hungry regional tyrant.
Chart the Military Regions
The struggle to unify the country both militarily and politically results chiefly due to the sheer, vast expanse of the Chinese nation. Under the Military Affairs Commission, the National Revolutionary Army is to divide its forces and regions of operation into twelve distinctive military regions (with overlap between provinces) to aid with military organisation.
March of the Red Army
For the first time in Chinese history, a nationalist and revolutionary army determined to liberate the Chinese people has succeeded in bringing about the unification of the Chinese country. Heroically we fight as we march to the sun of world revolution - we will continue on under the banner of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, with our comrades side by side, in bringing about the total liberation of all oppressed peoples.
The War of Resistance
Now our country faces perhaps its greatest danger in the history of Chinese civilisation, and we may face the complete annihilation of our race and culture if we do not act fast. Let us create a rallying call throughout the country for all of our Minzu to build a new Great Wall of flesh and blood to defend China from what may befall her: arise all ye who refuse to be slaves once more! March on!
Prepare Stay Behind Cells
Behind every blade of grass lies a Chinese peasant who is willing to carry his dadao and his rifle to wage war on the enemy. Even if we are forced to withdraw in the face of an overwhelming enemy, our partisans and bandits will wreck havoc behind enemy lines through sabotages and skirmishes. For every inch of soil we lose to the enemy, we will bite back.
Fortify the Coastal Bulwark
China's vast land expanse means that the enemy will most likely attempt a naval invasion of our country rather than a direct land invasion. Given the economic and political importance of the coastal regions, we would do well to prepare in advance of the enemy's invasion by fortifying and preparing the coastline with bunkers, pillboxes, and other defences.
Harness the Peoples' Will
It is the duty of every Chinese to stand up in the face of adversity, especially when the very existence of our people is threatened by imperialism. Too long have the Chinese proletariat been trampled by the boots of warlordism and imperialism; it is time for the Han race to remember their glorious heritage as the sons of Yan and Huang, and rise up together in patriotic unity to defend our Minzu!
Expand Mechanised Operations
European developments made by syndicalist officers such as Basil Liddel-Hart over the past few years have illustrated the importance of mechanised warfare in future battles and wars as a means of speed and breakthrough. Given the NRA's own favouritism of mobility and speed, some of our officer corps have proposed that we gradually adopt more experimental mechanised operations.
Examine Foreign Designs
It is no secret that while China certainly has the means and potential to fully embrace elements of a modern military such as mechanisation, actually doing so will definitely take a long while. We have long sought training and advice from the European syndicalist nations who are leading the world in armoured warfare, and we would do well to look to their designs for inspiration.
Domestic Armour Production
While we may recognise the superiority of European designs and concepts, European methods of armoured warfare are unsuitable for the terrain of the battles fought in China and across Asia. It will do us well to adopt and improvise by tapping into China's resources and formulating our own means of domestic armour production that may one day rival even the quality of Europe.
Forward Thinking Officer Corps
The future of any successful military lies not in its generals or its soldiers but rather the concepts and theories that drive progress within our own doctrine. With the return of the Kuomintang and the NRA's success in the Northern Expedition, some officers who stayed overseas in training have now returned with fresh, bold, and radical ideas on how to modernise the NRA.
The Modern Chinese Soldier
The warlords' armies were infamous worldwide for their apparent incompetence and lack of modern equipment. As part of our late Dr. Sun Yat-sen's plans to create a modern army, we take pride in our efforts to modernise the image of the Chinese soldier. Equipped with the latest rifles and imbued with the spirit of revolution, the rifleman of the NRA stands above all else!
Broad Front Operations Capacity
With the National Revolutionary Army reformed and larger than ever before, we are now able to adopt greater operational capacity on broader fronts. With improved reconnaissance units as well as a greater understanding of logistics and air power, the NRA will be able to undertake greater and larger campaigns than it was previously capable of.
Reinforce the Rearguard!
While our elite troops are distracted on the front lines, we should also take steps to ensure that the rear areas are secured. Despite the victory of the NRA in the Second Northern Expedition, there are plenty of regions within the country that are yet to be completely pacified. In order to maintain order and legitimacy, we will provide a greater deal of support to our rear guard forces.
The Soul of Whampoa
The Whampoa Military Academy is more than a mere military school; its mythos stems from the revolutionary spirit that floods its dorms and rooms. Whampoa is the bulwark of the national revolution, a source of strength for all Chinese to look up to. Despite hundreds of alumni becoming martyrs in the revolution, the future is bright for the next generation of Whampoa, the very soul of the national revolution.
