Revolutions are often a dance between dreams and nightmares. Beneath all the high-minded convictions the party holds, there is often a need for \
Found the Central Aviation School
Befitting China's war-torn, divided nature during the Warlord Era, many different warlord factions as well as the Zhili government sought to create their own air force to get an advantage over one another. These programmes were often too small and underfunded to be much good on their own, but if we were to bring them all together under one roof it could be the foundation of a real force multiplier for our armies.
Encourage the Doctrine of Initiative
The concept of initiative as a means of offence is one that is employed by the National Revolutionary Army, but it is also a concept that we will certainly apply to our own aerial programme. By encouraging our pilots to follow the European concepts of aerial initiative, we will have our fighters and bombers focus on more offensive capabilities rather than defensive ones.
Purchase Foreign Blueprints
While China certainly has the resources and capabilities to launch its own aerial development scheme, our technological progress in flight still lags years behind modern European designs. Years of exile in Europe have allowed us to test and examine European plane designs from the British Republican Air Force and the Communard Air Force. Let us purchase foreign blueprints and designs to create our own modern planes.
Flying Tigers
While our planes may certainly be inspired by European designs and help from the air came in the form of European volunteers, our efforts to create a native and solely Chinese air force is growing steadily, and with it, more and more pilots are claiming successes in the air day by day. Furthermore, we will also allow our revolutionary sisters to join us in the air to grow our air force.
The XP-0 Project
Based on the French fighter, the Loire L46, the XP-0 (developed by the officer Chu Chia-Jen) is China's first attempts at a native fighter prototype. Armed with 4x20 mm Hispano-Suiza underwing cannons and capable of carrying bombs as well, our goal for the XP-0 is to reduce our dependency on foreign purchased aircraft and instead foster pride and prestige with our own native aviation industry.
Encourage Attack Aviation
As shown in modern conflicts around the world, and especially by the world's major powers, the future of aviation lies in combined efforts with ground troops to launch decisive breakthroughs with an unprecedented level of firepower. Our flying students in Europe have witnessed attack bombers being used in European conflicts and are eager to share their knowledge with us.
Create the 9th Column
In a joint effort with the ROCAF and the NRA, an experimental division has been created of the most excellent and fit of our soldiers to serve in an elite unit. This brave unit is inspired by contemporary usage of paratroopers, allowing units to deploy into combat zones without land passage. While such tactics are radical and new with casualties to be expected, fortune favours the bold!
Master Air-Land Integration
The combination of aerial power and mechanised warfare combines the firepower of tactical and close air-support bombers with mobile troops. While the wars of the Warlord Era were fought with rifles and artillery, the future of modern warfare lies in an army's use of mobile artillery units in the form of direct air support to launch devastating offensives into the heart of the enemy.
Patrol the Coasts
While China's vast expanses connect us with the rest of Europe, her most industrial regions and sources of trade lie with the bountiful Chinese coastline. In times of war, an enemy with a stronger naval presence will certainly make an attempt to seize or blockade our vital sea lanes. In order to fight back, we will encourage the use of naval bombers to patrol and sink all who try!
Liberation from the Skies
Off into the clouds we fly up with our determination to defend our motherland, from the Kunlun Mountains to the shores of the Pacific Ocean. We fly over ranges, rivers, and majestic mountains determined to liberate the Chinese proletariat from the skies. Courageous and diligent, we strive to secure the prosperity of our civilisation forever with our air force!
Restore the Ministry of Navy
The Navy has ailed over the last few decades, forced to play a subservient role: a secondary priority compared to the army, an auxiliary force for foreign concessionists, and a money pit for our treasury. No more. If China is to be truly free, it must have a navy capable of defending its shores and protecting its trade. The first step is to create an independent command capable of overseeing its revival.
Salvage the Beiyang Fleet
Given we only have so many resources on hand, our limited production capacity, and the long construction time for new ships, it is best that make use of what our Beiyang predecessors have left us. Although much of it has been either stolen or is a smouldering wreck, there are still ships, facilities, and personnel that can reused for a much better purpose. Nothing is irreplaceable, but every bit helps.
Renovate the Jiangnan Dockyards
One of the most important naval facilities in the nation are the Jiangnan Dockyards. Forced to turn to civilian naval development to sustain its finances, now that we have successfully recovered Shanghai from foreign colonisers we will turn Jiangnan into the engine of a new, grander fleet of the Republic. An influx of investment will recruit new staff, create new dry-docks, and above all produce new ships.
New Navy, New Traditions
Tradition is important in life, but there are few places where it is of such significance as aboard the fleet. Even as China's naval capacity shrank, the fleet remains divided into various competing regional cliques. With a steady hand, we shall fuse them into one Chinese fleet, infused with the enlightenment of the Three Principles and combining the lessons learned across the nation. This is how we shall win.
Commission the Six Year Programme
The dreams of the revolutionaries often outstrip the government's actual ability to realise them. Nonetheless, when the party stated its goal of developing a capacity of 600,000 tons in 6 years, the Navy went full steam ahead with its plans. Working tirelessly day and night, hundreds of ships are ordered, though admittedly few are above 500 tons. We are witnessing the birth of a new Chinese fleet.
Fleet of the Republic
The new republic needs a new fleet capable of defending its shores. With investments already underway and lost years slowly recovered, the once withered and divided Chinese fleet has been reborn. Already a new fleet is taking shape, capable of taking on foes it once had no choice but to cower from. We are a long way from becoming a great maritime power again, but our star continues to rise!
Prepare the Coastal Garrison Plan
China's long coastline is a major vulnerability in the event of foreign invasion, as prior wars have demonstrated. Although the land-based defences are in the army's domain, the fleet also has a responsibility to keep invaders off our shores and harry those foolish enough to try. With adequate early-warning systems and crafty tactics, we can strike our foes at their weakest by the coast.
Death from the Depths
Beneath the surface in the darkest depths, intrepid men in deadly vessels lurk. Submarine warfare was in its infancy in the previous war, but has since become an equaliser between the haughty fleets of the status quo and the states that they oppress. We shall make full use of these technologies to raid enemy supply convoys supplying their invasion forces, and also pick off any vulnerable capital ships.
Coastal Defence Stratagems
It is not enough to simply know where our foes will be arriving. We must develop an arm of light ships capable of disrupting enemy attacks - using speed, ingenuity and above all daring to strike. These coastal defence ships must be cheap and designed for China's coast, laying various traps and coordinating with the ground to gain an advantage over our foes more expensive vessels. Likewise, they must be able to protect our own shipping.
Blockade Runners
It is unfortunately a reality we face, that for all of our efforts we will only at best be able to protect areas in the immediate vicinity of our coastline. Outside of our fortified harbours and far away from even our strike-planes, it is likely our foes will attempt to cut off major shipments using their naval superiority. We must develop strategies and crafts capable of evading enemy patrols and breaking the blockade.
Consolidate Maritime Peace
If we are to bring prosperity back to our nation, we must work to calm the seas and bring back harmony to the waters. This means creating a force capable of protecting our trade from foreign thieves, defending the nation's commerce in our waters. We shall reinforce our Navy and Coast Guard's defensive capabilities, making them adept at shielding our precious cargo in the event of war.
Look towards the Three Seas
China's destiny belongs not merely on the land but also across the three seas that surround it. Moreover, there are so many other peoples across Asia that yearn for liberation from colonial powers, and it is only by developing a fleet capable of challenging these oppressors that China can resume its leadership role for the continent. Our armies march, and our fleet will support them all the way.
Integrate Naval-Air Coordination
Naval Aviation is a field that has made great strides over the last few decades. While it might be premature to believe us capable of such operations given our limited air and sea capabilities, we have an advantage over our more established peers in our lack of entrenched doctrines. Therefore, we must be willing to have flexibility, bringing both our naval and air assets together in a deadly combination.
Invite Foreign Naval Advisors
We are not alone in this world, and we do not need to reinvent the wheel. Therefore, with the help of our allies in Europe and various independent experts we have hired from foreign fleets, we can enhance our own naval capabilities in a timely manner. Using designs purchased or \
\
The Marine Corps of the Republic of China are about as old as the Republic itself. Built from the ashes of the old Navy Sentry Corps in 1914, various commanders including Sa Zhenbing hoped to create a force trained in amphibious landings after seeing the potency of the invading Eight-power alliance. The Fujian fleet has also sponsored large detachments of naval infantry. Together, they shall be the basis of a force capable of projecting abroad.
Embrace the Surface Fleet Doctrine
New technologies in the air and beneath the sea are fascinating, but in the end of the day control of the water is determined by the surface fleet. And China has been without a competent one for far too long. We shall build a new armada capable of dominating the waves, bringing to heel those of the Japanese, Germans, and any others who dare to menace Asia.
Chinese Grand Fleet
It is not enough for us to be satisfied with petty gunboats and outdated cruisers. A real fleet requires capital ships, those capable of shredding apart enemy escorts and bombarding enemy fortifications. If we are serious about our naval ambitions, we must be willing to invest in the pricey grand vessels worth of great powers. We are living in the dawn of a new age in the Pacific, and may we be at the centre.
A World Set Free
Henceforth with the success of the liberation wars - there shall be no nations and no borders. With the success of the fourth stage of revolution, that is the revolution for all peoples, we have brought a natural accordance between the groundbreaking words of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and those expressed by the great thinkers such as Proudhon. Truly, we can now finally declare a federation amongst all peoples - to live in harmony and love forevermore.
Action Now!
The moment came and Song Qingling took it - the Kuomintang's budding dictator Wang Jingwei was ousted from power and a new government has been formed to guide China forward. Her Provisional Action Committee has truly lived up to its name, taking charge in China's darkest hour. However, they did not do it alone, and they might find that taking power is one thing while governing is another...
Rally the Peoples' Militias!
The PAC-trained militia in the MinGan Insurgent Zone have long been the core of the national revolution; now, when the revolution needs them the most, we must call them to action. Let us rally militia forces across the country to help secure the revolution from the counter-revolutionaries who will seek to destroy all we have fought for. Rise up comrades, the time is now!
Promises of Democracy
It is the duty of the Provisional Action Committee to inspire direct action by implementing local forms of self-government, led by PAC leaders to ensure that they remain safe from the allure of radicalism and to liberate them from years of instability and government corruption. The Provisional Action Committee of the Kuomintang seeks to use the party as an organ for the eventual democratisation of Chinese society.
Utilise Military Connections
The Guanxi Policy is the system of loyalty and revolutionary unity between the hero of the revolution, Deng Yanda, and his close associates. Through an elaborate network of interpersonal relationships among its leaders, PAC members are expected to follow these exemplary men and women, led by General Deng Yanda, to save the revolution. In times of crisis, certain individuals are gifted with the skills necessary for revolution.
Initiate Land to the Tiller
The Provisional Action Committee adheres to the model of land reform given to us by the late Dr. Sun. All lands of the evil gentry, warlords, and foreign imperialists shall be returned to the people, we shall pursue the nationalisation of land while also granting the rights and ownership of land to those who work it. Furthermore, land rent caps are to be established and village associations formed to protect peasant interests.
Fate of the CRS
The China Revival Society's hold on our army's radical ranks, as well as their totalitarian and reactionary ideals, cannot be tolerated by the Party. Nonetheless, some of them were our comrades in Whampoa and perhaps there is use for them yet. There is always the question of figures such as Dai Chunfeng, who seem amicable to cooperation. Perhaps they may offer us rewards and secrets for amnesty.
Reconcile the RCA
Members of Wang's former Reorganisation Comrades Associates hold less radical and authoritarian views than do the radical members of his clique. Led by Gu Mengyu, the RCA's Moderate wing opposes ideas of class conflict and shares our ideals on the matter of land reform. With our leadership of the Party solidified, let us seek to reintegrate them back into the Party as formal party members with their rights restored.
The Red Napoleon
The National Revolution would have been aborted once more had it not been for General Deng Yanda. The talented Deng, whose intellect and selflessness matches no other, is not only a national hero for his role in the revolution but may also be Song Qingling's most trusted voice within the Kuomintang. It is by Deng's voice that the revolution breathes, and it is with Deng's leadership that we will strive for glory.
Empower Rural Cooperatives
With the help of the Kuomintang, the Party is to aid in organising rural associations and cooperatives among the peasantry in order to foster the roots for a good and nurtured democracy. These cooperatives will help them realise the goals of minquan and minsheng with the assistance of the Party's leadership, to strengthen their revolutionary consciousness while also providing for their own needs and freedom from the risk of famines.
Exalt the Struggle of Pingmin
The Chinese workers and peasants form the true people of China, long oppressed by foreign imperialists, corrupt warlords, and local bullies for their labour and lives. There is no greater and more admirable cause than that of the Chinese peasants and workers who toil, labour, and suffer under the excesses of imperialism. Now, with the success of the revolution, we strive towards their full liberation.
Revolution by the Chinese Method
It is in accordance with our understanding and belief that the national revolution must be done in the Chinese method, that is, the idea of the dangguo (party-state). There is no other political situation akin to China's, and it is only through firm leadership and organisation that the Second Northern Expedition was successful. The revolution must be done in this way until the time is ready.
Encourage Revolutionary Thought
Through pamphlets, radio broadcasts, lectures, and rallies we will encourage the youth to study Dr. Sun's Three Principles of the People and to learn about the Party's history. In the schools and universities of this nation, we must teach them to seek liberation and modernity and to break away from old superstitions. After all, this new China belongs to them.
Consolidate the WMARCA
During one of the Party's most pivotal moments, it was the brave and stalwart generals of the WMARCA who helped save it from collapse. The National Revolutionary Army shall be made up of those in the WMARCA, to serve in fraternal and revolutionary roles as protectors of the ideals of the national revolution. Doing so will further strengthen the NRA as an army for the Party.
In Pursuit of Datong
What we strive for is the goal of datong, the great unity, and the China of the future is to be a socialist datong society. There will be no money, no warfare, no family, no prison, and no religion. From each according to his ability, to each according to his needs - the Three Principles are merely a means to reach this equal society. The Chinese National Revolution, is after all, not merely a political revolution but also a truly social revolution.
Pingmin Zhengquan
The end goal of the Chinese National Revolution is socialism; the Chinese revolution exemplifies characteristics of national revolution, democratic revolution, and eventually social revolution. However, this process is not a fast one and must be done in the Chinese method. Democracy and socialism must be nurtured and watered by the Party's leadership so that the masses may grow to understand and become the leadership of the social revolution that is to come.
Convene the People's Congress
The Party has to lead and convene a new Congress, one for the common people of China. The peasants and workers are to form the core of our new government, a broad united front of workers, peasants, women, soldiers, and other professional organisations that can elect representatives to a hierarchy of assemblies who shall exercise true power. At last, the true people of China have stood up, and it is only fitting that a new Congress represents their interests.
Revolution for All Peoples
Unlike the radicals who declare that only class revolution is necessary for national liberation, Dr. Sun Yat-sen believed in revolution for the common people - including the intellectual, worker, peasant, and merchant classes. This is clearly stated in the declaration of the Kuomintang's First Congress, that the national revolution be a revolution for all peoples - working together to achieve the great unity, side by side.
Workplace Democracy
In the future socialist society that is to come, the distinctions between intellectuals, workers, peasants, and merchants will cease to exist, as everyone will labour for society. In order to meet the needs of production, these labourers will organise themselves into a variety of groups, win which all men and women will have equal say in the affairs of their organisations and their production.
Minsheng Geming
According to Li Shizeng, progress manifests in history through four political stages: the monarchical revolution, the revolution for people's sovereignty, the class revolution, and finally the revolution for world unity - the revolution for the people's livelihood, for social revolution, and for great unity. This particular social revolution shall be one based on the great ideals of Proudhon and Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings.
Towards Devolution
In order to reach datong, a hierarchy of units of government, from towns to regional councils, and finally to the Central Government, is to exist so that regional power is distributed and able to freely develop. This is a temporary stage; while the existence of the Party in maintaining the military and economy persists, it is necessary only until the eventual abolition of government.
Towards a Dream of True Love
\
National Labour University
The National Labour University is the brainchild of the anarchist Cai Yuanpei and is inspired by the University of Labourers in Charleroi, Belgium. Its primary goal is to combine labour and learning to create a new kind of individual, the intellectual labourer. Considered by the anarchists within the Party as the first step in the revolutionising of Chinese education, the goal is to eradicate distinctions between classes and to train the next generation of labour leaders.
Strengthen the Unions
While we seek the eventual eradication of social classes in Chinese society in the form of revolutionary groups, these groups cannot be established overnight. Hence, when the revolution comes about, there will be chaos without organisation. As such, it is imperative that we look to working with existing syndicates and unions and have the workers of the country unite and become the forefront of the social revolution that is to come.
Collaboration of the Oppressed Classes
Unlike the radicals in the RCA or the Chinese Syndicalist Party that believe that class war is inevitable, we acknowledge that class is merely an expression of selfish interests and an obstacle to the realisation of a humane society. Those who advocate for class struggle seek only the interests of a single class, while the task of revolution given to us is to put such thoughts behind, relegated to the past forevermore; boldly, we move towards the notion of an anarchist and free society.
The Two-Stage Revolution
Many of us share the belief that while China is a semi-feudal country and not a completely feudal nation, the emphasis of the Chinese Revolution should be placed on national unity and unification first, before the social revolution. It is the platform of the CSP-Orthodox wing to work with the Chinese Kuomintang in order to establish a leading vanguard of intellectuals and leaders to lead China into the transition from the first to the second stage.
Groundwork for the Proletarian Future
In order to elide the contradictions between the Marxist theory of worker-peasant alliance and the reality of such an alliance, we must equate the notion of the syndicalist movement with the working class, and the leadership of the peasant movement with the proletariat proper. The Party must advance its goals of creating a proletarian class of labourers who shall take the leading position in the Party's movement, as proof of inevitable proletarian hegemony.
Initiate the Consultative Conference
Following the victory of the Unity Government in saving the revolution from the hands of former Chairman Wang Jingwei, it is only fitting that we invite delegates from the various Republican and liberal political factions who are interested in working with the Kuomintang to ensure the growth of democracy in China. A conference is to be initiated to discuss the plans and designs for the revived Party and the future national constitution.
Legalise Democratic Parties
During the necessary phase of political tutelage, it was important that the Kuomintang remain the sole organ of political and revolutionary activity due to the chaos and weakness of having a loose political structure, especially given the military nature of the National Revolution. With the country finally and fully united, there is no longer any need for the Kuomintang to be the sole party of the revolution.
Guarantee Constitutional Freedoms
The late Dr. Sun Yat-sen, in his writings on the notion of minquan or the people's governance, believed that all people are entitled to four basic democratic rights: the rights to election, the rights to initiative, the rights to referendum, and the rights to recall. Under the Judicial and Legislative Yuans, we will pass judgement and approve basic laws to guarantee the rights of the people so that democracy may finally grow in China.
The Third Stage of Revolution
Dr. Sun Yat-sen designed the revolution to occur in three great stages: the first being the military phase of the revolution in which martial law is needed, the second being the stage of transitional democracy in which the Party is to help encourage the exercise of political rights for the people. We are now in the third stage of this revolution, in which reconstruction can be completed and the need for political tutelage is no longer a requirement for governance.
Court Liberal Intellectuals
Liberals such as Hu Shih have long criticised the Chinese Nationalist Party for our so-called betrayal of constitutionalism and for the Party's adoption of party-state rule in order to train the masses. As we soften our stance on the party-state and tutelage, let us reach out to these liberals and fellow intellectuals to remove the barriers of ideological thought and to pursue a genuine, unified road towards liberalism.
Honouring Revolutionary Martyrs
We will never forget the martyrs of our nation and Party who helped pave the road for our revolution to succeed. Great leaders and patriots such as Liao Zhongkai and Chiang Kai-shek shall forever be remembered as heroes in the revolutionary cause to free our country. Furthermore, we must also bring back the body of Dr. Sun from [GetVictoryPointName_9843] to a rightful resting place in Nanjing.
Rein in the Military
For a long time, Chinese politics and especially the politics of the Kuomintang have been dominated by the military due to the complex and unstable nature of the Chinese political scene. With national unification achieved and domestic counter-revolutionaries subdued, there is no longer any need for the military to play a large role in politics. It is time to curb the excess of military leadership by placing limits on those who can partake in the civilian government.
Promote Local Self-Government
It is the goal of the Party that the eventual education and training of the masses will allow local regions to establish successfully-functioning local governments. Although the government shall still be central in nature, we will encourage the growth of democratic principles at a grass-roots level, allowing regional leaders to execute decisions and ideas without the intervention of the central government.
Promote Nationalist Youth Organisations
It is important that the youth of our nation learn to love our nation's ten thousand years of cultural supremacy, as well as for them to remember the martyrs and heroes of the National Revolution. By consolidating and forming boys' and girls' scouting and political organisations, we will encourage membership in this youth organisations to promote the values of the Three Principles of the People to China's next generation.
The Vision of the Eternal Premier
The late Dr. Sun believed that democracy was the end goal of the National Revolution, but that democracy and nationalism must grow together under the leadership of a Party that aims to train and grow a revolutionary peoples into a revolutionary nation. At last, we have reached the stage of revolution where we are finally able to achieve this democracy - as such, we have successfully completed and honoured the Late Premier's Will and Testament.
Heir to the Revolution
In the revolution's gravest hour, the reactionaries and anti-revolutionaries sought to dismantle the National Revolution, but Chairman Wang has stood firm. With power now fully consolidated in the Central Committee and the Party, the Chairman may now finally seek to exercise and fulfil Dr. Sun's will.
Pacify the Reactionary Opposition
Chairman Wang has led the Kuomintang through the last several years, effectively transforming it from an exiled organisation to the Nationalist Party that has unified China according to the ideals of the late Dr. Sun. However, after the Third Congress, there have been those who have sought to dismantle everything the Chairman has built and now, with the Chairman's hold secured, either amnesty or punishment must be dealt to those who have rebelled.
The Theatrical Revolutionary State
To revitalise support throughout the nation and the Party, it is imperative that the Reorganisation Comrades Association incorporate elements of traditional theatrical dramas in portraying the party's history with Wang taking the leading role. Through the spectacle of the arts, we will connect the glorious past of the Chinese Republic and Dr. Sun with our very own revolution and our time spent under Chairman Wang.
Our Comrades in the CSP
Over the years, we have participated in a rather symbiotic relationship with the League of Chinese Syndicalists and the various syndicalist groups within the league as part of the United Front policy. With the National Revolution finally successful, the time has come to reevaluate our relationship with the Chinese Syndicalists and to perhaps sway the influence of one of their factions in order to strengthen our broad national support.
Commence the National Land Reform
Per the instructions and doctrine left behind to us from our beloved, late, eternal Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Kuomintang is to embrace the mass movement by commencing the land reform movement in order to help end feudalism and push Chinese society towards the social revolution. RCA ideologues Gu Mengyu and Chen Gongbo have brought their unique ideas to the table, and have presented their designs for the Chairman to consider as the official party agenda for land reform.
Revolutionary Pragmatism
What makes the Chairman unique amongst the leaders of the Kuomintang is his own doctrine of revolutionary pragmatism that allows him to balance the multiple cliques within his own followers. His pragmatism is also expressed in his own ambivalence towards Chen Jiongming and the Federalists as well as his willingness to subvert the nationalistic ideals of the KMT in favour for economic and military aid from the Third Internationale.
Towards Radical Reorganisation
The Chairman has not forgotten the years of loyalty given to him by his trusted right-hand man Chen Gongbo. While he is not formally a member of the Reorganisation Comrades Association, by empowering the Radical Faction of the RCA the Chairman has committed himself to the platform of Chen Gongbo and his more radical ideas in dealing with the chaos of reorganising the party following the Third Congress.
Reorganise the Political Department
The Political Department of the NRA has long been nominally aligned to us over the Provisional Action Committee, giving us much-needed influence within the Whampoa Military Academy due to most of the school being loyal to PAC. With our hold secured, it is time for us to thoroughly reorganise the entire party. We will encourage only socialist- and Marxist-inspired thoughts in the Political Department to ensure that Chinese students will be the future vanguard.
Venerate Class Struggle
It is the platform of the RCA-Radicals that class struggle is the only means of achieving social revolution and that the materialist social revolution is an inevitable result of the Chinese National Revolution. With the success of national unification, it is only natural that we encourage the peasants and workers to rise up and break their chains, so that we may draw closer to a society free of class strife.
Nurture the Revolutionary Future
As the late Eternal Premier instructed us, the future belongs to the youth and the strength of the revolution depends on our care and instruction of China's next generation. Let us create a socialist youth corps, dedicated to the idea of loyalty to the Chinese nation and to the Chairman so that we may prepare the next generation to maintain the revolution.
Discipline the RCA
The Reorganisation Comrades Association, while certainly the core base of those who align and support the legitimacy of Chairman Wang, are nonetheless too ambitious for their own good. There is no doubt that the RCA seeks to merely draw Wang away from his important matters and his own political ideology. It is imperative that we begin to crackdown on this radical movement, as their talks of revolution merely alienate popular support for the current regime.
Lead the New Citizens Movement
The New Citizens Movement seeks to encourage the youth and all other oppressed groups to study the Three Principles of the People and to look towards the May 30th strikes as an example of the future. The movement will seek to incorporate the study of the Three Principles' of the People, emphasise industrial prowess, and eradicate corrupt thinking. It is through this movement that comrades will be taught to faithfully follow and obey the will of the Chairman.
Achieve Workers' Democracy
It is the aim for the Chairman and the Reorganisation Comrades Association that tutelage will come to an end one day, and that there will truly be democracy in China. However, the democracy envisioned by those within the RCA is that of a democracy run by the masses - that is, the workers and peasants of the Natural Revolution. Let us seek to empower unions and councils to prepare the groundwork for a revolutionary future.

The Chairman's Right Hand
Truly, Chen Gongbo is a remarkable man. There is none other within the Party that more effectively conveys his speeches and his support for the Chairman's policies than him. While those who oppose him argue that Chen is merely a modern day Cao Cao, it is undisputable that Chen is the right hand of the Chairman. The Chairman has no doubts regarding Chen Gongbo's loyalty, and it is with this trust that the RCA will be able to expand their operations farther than ever before.
Empowering the Presidential Camarilla
The events of the Third Congress showed the Chairman that factionalism within the Party only seeks to cripple and destabilise the Party rather than uphold it. It is only fitting that power is delegated regionally to those who have been with Wang since the very beginning - those who know him best and whom he trusts, no matter what. As such, the bureaucracy of the Party shall be staffed by those within Wang's inner circle.
Subvert the RCA
Long has the Reorganisation Comrades Association been a thorn in the progress of our Chairman's revolution. Their talks of revolution, of Marxism, of historical materialism do nothing but further divide our Party and their stance on class struggle is contrary to the ideals set before us by the Guofu; the late leader believed that the revolution should be for all people, not just the workers. It is past time that we help put the RCA in its place.
Treasure the Memory of the Guofu
Dr. Sun Yat-sen - the revolutionary pioneer, brilliant statesman, generalissimo, teacher, philosopher, and eternal premier - is truly the Guofu of this country. While he was unable to witness himself the success of the Northern Expedition, let us remember forever that it is with Dr. Sun's ideals that we carry out the nature of revolution and have shown that his methods are indeed necessary to achieve victory.
No Reconstruction Without Peace
Chen Bijun or Madame Wang has written that there can be no effective National Reconstruction until there is peace in this country. As long as subversive elements and reactionary dissidents exist within the Party there will be no peace, no harmony within the Party's functions. It is thus the duty of the Residence Faction to ensure that the Party is cleansed of that which must be removed.
Emulate the French Education Model
We have learned a lot from our dear brothers and sisters of the revolutionary cause in France, including how they have handled the concepts of public education, of research universities, and of workers' education. It is fitting that, in a country struggling with literacy, we adopt educational institutions akin to those in Europe for modernisation.
Promise an End to Party Factionalism
The events of the Third National Congress have proved that the Chairman's writings are right, as they showed that factionalism can truly lead to the decay and degeneration of the party. It is the duty of the Chairman and those who support him to end all notions of factionalism - to crush cliques and secret organisations, to enforce a line of party unity.
The Second Sun Yat-sen
Within the Chinese Nationalist Party, there is none more faithful and committed to the cause and ideals of the late Dr. Sun than Wang Jingwei - his ever-loyal disciple and follower. And it has been Wang who has led the Party from near destruction into exile, and then a triumphant return with the success of the Second Northern Expedition and the War of Resistance. Indeed, the Chairman alone is the true successor of our late Eternal Premier.
Promises of a Provisional Constitution
The military phase of the National Revolution has concluded, and the period of political tutelage shall soon have to end. As such, before the phase of tutelage is fully concluded, according to the Chairman, it is necessary that a provisional constitution be drafted so that the rights and liberties of the people may be guaranteed as soon as possible. Inspired by the Moderates of the RCA, this constitution shall seek to cover all peoples - not just the workers and peasants.

The Chairman's Will
The recent events in Nanjing and Fujian have shown that the National Revolution is still yet to be fully secured. In order to maintain the revolutionary fervour and strength of the Second Northern Expedition, it is imperative that the Chairman's powers continue to be executive in order to promote the effectiveness of the Party. He shall lead us with absolute power and authority, as only he is fit to carry the mantle of the late Dr. Sun.
Pursue the Deradicalisation Line
Since the Party's founding, the Party has been committed to a policy of anti-imperialism. Yet while we supported the turn to the left during the 1924 Reorganisation of the Party, the masses of the national revolution ought to be controlled rather than encouraged. In order to prevent the excesses of revolution, let us seek to tone down the anti-imperialist and revolutionary rhetoric.
Technocratic Administration
The Party is in need of serious reform, and the bureaucrats of the Party's administrations must be swapped in favour of those with more moderate stances than those of the RCA-Radicals. Radicalism threatens to destroy everything that we have built and we would do well to rectify this by employing intellectuals and politicians who are good at what they do, rather than mere ideologues.
Guide the Producer Classes
The Chairman believes that the democratic forces will be the key to success in winning the hearts and minds of the Chinese people during the National Revolution. These forces will be made up of the producer classes; that is, those of the workers, peasants, intellectuals, students, and other occupations. It is through the leadership of the Party that these classes will strive for democracy to support their own interests - helping China as a whole democratise.
Towards Local Self-Government
According to the Chairman, local self-government begins when the Party helps to organise occupational groups made up of the local peasantry, workers, and petite bourgeoisie. These groups are then encouraged to set up local assemblies, where they could help reflect their communities' best interests and advance in fulfilling shared goals alongside each other through this effective system of close cooperation.
The Federalist Compromise
There are certainly many within the Party who will never forgive Chen Jiongming and his Federalists for nearly jeopardising the life of our late leader and the revolution. However, the PIP has shown that they are willing to work with us, and the Chairman is pragmatic enough to invite them to partake in the national revolution. Let us seek to put aside petty differences for the sake of the greater goal - the goal of national democracy.
Concept of the Exceptional Individual
Unlike the Radicals, the Moderates of the RCA do not believe in the role of social or economic environments in driving history, but rather the will of the individual. Revolutionaries should not place blind faith in the masses, but rather should place their hopes upon exceptional individuals, leaders such as Chairman Wang, to lead the masses in the revolution. The quality of individuals in the national revolution dictates whether or not the revolution will succeed or fail.
Subordinate the Army to the Party
The Chairman believes that the Army must always be subservient to the Party. To control the Party, the Chairman has recommended that the commissariat system and political indoctrination within the army be actively used. Furthermore, all administrative decisions for the army must be made by Party Centre. The army must serve the desires of the people and the Party; in this way can years of militarism in China finally be cured.
The Necessity of Dangguo
While the Chairman is committed to a platform of democracy, democracy must still be nurtured and watered with the guidance of the Party. The Party is effective in weeding out anti-revolutionaries and is the embodiment of the oppressed peoples; as such, it is capable of leading people in the revolutionary struggle. Furthermore, the people have lived too long under autocratic rule, and the Party is needed to guide them and prepare them for democracy to come.
Ensure the Four Basic Rights
It was the late leader's idea that the Chinese people and masses would be able to utilise the four rights of election, recall, referendum, and initiative. The Party is to play a great role in this process, by aiding and training the masses to exercise these rights. Even as the §RRCA§! and the §SPAC§! slug it out for dominance, smaller groups pursue their own agenda and vie for influence. §rThe stronger each are, the more impact they will have in deciding the victor of revolution-long power-struggle§!. They may also influence the options available to the ultimate winner, cementing their role in Chinese history.\n\nThe §lReconstruction Faction§! represents the rump liberal bloc within the party. Their insistence on constitutionalism and moderation has endeared some, but attracted accusations of being a front for the meddling of the urban and overseas elite. Secure OCC Donations
Revolution and nation often makes for strange bedfellows. Despite our socialist ideals, there are many wealthy sympathisers willing to provide lavish donations to our cause, either out of a nationalistic desire to cast out foreign imperialism or perhaps out of hope of endearing themselves to our administration. Most are affiliated with either the Legations-based Vermillion Society or with the Overseas Chinese Commission (OCC), based in wealthy Chinese expatriate communities in Southeast Asia and the United States. Indeed, quite a few leading Kuomintang figures were born to such families such as Sun Fo, Chen Youren, and Chen Bijun. While we might not always see eye to eye, and they surely hope our leftist beliefs are simply a phase, the donations we receive are very real.
Utilise Underground Networks
After the collapse of the Northern Expedition, many National Revolutionary officers went underground. In this time, the lines between rebellion and crime often blurred, with Kuomintang smuggling networks frequently overlapping with organised crime. Even as we transition towards a more legitimate mode of governance, the realities of war mean that weapons procurement is often an unsavoury business. Tapping into the connections we have and building more of them might mean the difference between a new China and broken dreams.
Stoke Military Fanaticism
Ever since the first days of Whampoa, the National Revolutionary Army has been trained to be utterly and fanatically loyal to the party and its revolutionary cause. This fanaticism separated it from the warlords it fought, and the Whampoa myth began with the battle of Mianhu during the Eastern Expedition against Chen Jiongming's forces. Outnumbered 20 to 3, two regiments of Whampoa graduates suffered nearly 70% casualties in the battle but nonetheless carried the day - routing their opponents. It is just as important to keep the Whampoa spirit alive today, breeding the revolutionary enthusiasm that has created countless martyrs and heroes over the decades. United in fraternity, devotion, and sincerity, we march forward to national salvation!
Rally Industrial Workers
China's industry is primarily concentrated by the coast, including the Five Provinces. And, the workers there have been ceaselessly exploited by foreign concessionists and their Chinese lackeys. As they sweated and suffered, discontent grew and born from this anger is our revolution. Having shattered the chains that bound the proletariat, we must ask them to continue to sacrifice - but not for the petty benefit of greedy foreign capitalists but for their Chinese brethren. Through their sacrifice a new China is built.
Secure Internationale Technical Aid
Although they may be a world away, our socialist brothers and sisters abroad remain a critical source of technical aid. Through research sharing programmes, research grants for our scientists, and loans for our development foreign sponsorship has given us a critical advantage to help keep pace with other internationally backed rivals in China. One day we will modernise to the point we will once more be a beacon of scientific progress for the world, but for now we will take the assistance as needed.
Sponsor Cultural Institutions
Culture is an integral part to what makes a nation, and as we work to build a revived China we must also revive its culture. Although there is plenty of ongoing discourse as to what a socialist Chinese culture ought to look like, there is little doubt that revolution should not mean a lack of beauty or vibrancy. After all, the arts and humanities are for all to share - peasants and workers alike. Providing adequate funding for museums, universities, and other institutions show that we are enlightened rulers.
Support the Revolution in Indochina
The heroic peoples in Indochina have uprose against their German occupiers! The Germans came in to replace the French after the Great War and have proven little better - forcing the natives to toil in their plantations while capitalists exploit all the profits. It is from this foothold (and others) that the Germans continued to expand their presence: into the British colonies post-collapse and then into China in 1927. Should revolutionary groups succeed here, it would deal a devastating blow to German prestige and help avenge their intervention in the Northern Expedition!
Disband the Liberation Forces
Although idealistic in nature and a part of our quest to cast out foreign imperialism, the various liberation forces we have recruited have since served their purpose and ought to be disbanded. We will collect their weapons from them and send their officers and men home, with a small degree of pomp and fanfare.
Forming the Korean Volunteer Corps
Despite the loss of the Korean nation to Japanese imperialism since 1910, many loyal Korean nationalists and patriots still hold true - the dream of a free and democratic Korean nation. We share the same struggle of anti-imperialism as the Korean peoples and our own conflict with Japan is inevitable in order to free China from the chains of imperialism. As such, we will encourage the formation of a Korean Volunteer Corps led by the former Whampoa alumni Kim Wonbong, so that when the time comes - we will be able to help our Korean comrades achieve their long awaited liberation.
Forming the Three Stars Army
The peoples of Malaysia have been under the oppressive thumb of a series of colonisers and after the British revolution the Germans exploited the opportunity to seize the area for themselves. The brave freedom-fighters there have not submitted so easily. As our troops move into the region, we could secure some critical allies for ourselves - if only we would ask.
Freeing the Nations of Indochina
Indochina was handled over to the German boot as a spoil of war after the French defeat in the Great War. We have long held ties with the anti-imperialist insurgents, and now that our armies have moved into the area we must take care to ensure we are seen as liberators rather than another occupier. This however, might be easier said than done...
Fund the Japanese People's Emancipation League
Not all of the Japanese are militarist imperialists. Formed by those who have defected so far as well as Japanese socialists, the Japanese People's Emancipation League (JPEL) under Nosaka Sanzō seeks to re-educate Japanese prisoners of wars and to win our trust and friendship. They seek to establish a democratic people's government in post-war Japan and we should support their efforts in psychological warfare to dismantle the Japanese war effort.

GFX_CHI_intro
The MinGan Insurgency
In the late winter of 1927, the Chinese Nationalist Party (Kuomintang)'s National Revolution was on the brink of collapse following a series of major military defeats and the death of the expedition's commander §PChiang Kai-shek§!. With the destruction of the Kuomintang's National Revolutionary Army (NRA), §lGeneral Li Jishen§! convinced a part of the NRA to continue the revolution by waging a protracted war of resistance against the §PZhili warlords§! and their German lackeys. He was joined by §SSong Qingling§! and later §SDeng Yanda§!, and after the failure of their §r1932 Shanghai Uprising§! they decided to flee for the remote mountainous villages and forests of southeastern Jiangxi and northwestern Fujian, hoping to one day strike back. Meanwhile, the §RCentral Committee of the Kuomintang§!, dominated by the Party's left wing, fled for Europe - hoping to organise a government of exile to perhaps one day liberate China.\n\nHere in the remote rural backwater of southern China, §SSong Qingling's§! populist-based government has created a unique movement shrouded in secrecy- one with ties to cells and allied towns in the region. Peasants (both men and women) are trained and taught by NRA officers, hoping to inspire a new generation of revolutionaries - capable of fulfilling the mission of national salvation. They are taught that there shall be no class and chains in the Kuomintang's free China. They are further aided by a vast network of spies, informants, party cells, and fellow leftists in the Shanghai Neutral Zone - with rumours of §oeven criminal organisations§! playing a role in arms smuggling and supplies.\n\nIn 1932, Chinese syndicalists, socialists, and members of the Kuomintang staged mass strikes across the eastern seaboard of China - hoping to cripple the despicable §PLeague of Eight Provinces§!. While brutally repressed, it has given hope and faith to those in China - perhaps the Kuomintang may return once more.

But like the zodiac, the same cycles of poverty and exploitation continue on. And like rats, Kuomintang insurgents remain underground in hiding, festering in their squalor.\n\nBut they continue to survive nonetheless. The repeated \

Fallout of the ZheGan Railway Purchase
For all the sins of the imperialists and concessionists, sloth is not one of them. Exploiting cheap Chinese labour (and a token Chinese representation among the engineers), the Aufsichtsrat der Ostasiatischen Generalverwaltung (AOG) have built a large railway extending from Shanghai to Nanchang. The AOG is an extension of German concessionism, an arm for corporate conglomerates hoping to exploit Chinese resources. Their move into Jiangxi (the heart of MinGan), paying numerous bribes and braving our best efforts to stop them, has been a source of despair as they brushed aside sabotage and corruption alike.\n\nBut in many ways, perhaps that same determined avarice is the capitalists' downfall. Betraying their local partners and any promises of a more egalitarian future, scandal broke out when the AOG suddenly announced their decision to consolidate their controlling shares in various Chinese railways into one on behalf of the Schantung-Eisenbahn-Gesellschaft (an AOG subsidiary).\n\nThis move to entrench German dominance and force Chinese managers to answer to a German board has backfired, with widespread anger boiling over across the League. The ZheGan railway, once a much advertised sign of progress, has now become a symbol of the continued humiliation of the Chinese people. It seems the Germans have forgotten their history - it was not long ago that a similar rail dispute in China set forth the fall of an empire...
Our dear country moans under the weight of imperialism!
Capitalism must be driven out of our nation once and for all!
The Brewing Tempest
The Kuomintang, once on the back-foot amidst the League's advance, has seen new life breathed into its lungs. The much vaunted ZheGan railway project has awoken decades of pent up anger among the long-suffering Chinese people. With waves of condemnation coming from concerned intellectuals, socialist factory pamphlets, and nationalist publications of all stripes, it seems that the scandal has struck a deep nerve across a broad section of Chinese society.\n\nThe spark of resistance has spread like wildfire. In cities both in the League and elsewhere, there have been widespread protests and boycotts against the AOG. Railroads have been attacked and sabotaged, and League authorities (themselves said to be fuming over the Germans' betrayal) have been slow to stop them. Various officials and foreign citizens said to be tied to ZheGan have been attacked by mobs and some assassinated in the anti-concessionist frenzy.\n\nWhile Kuomintang and other socialist insurgents can claim credit for some of them, they are not even close to a majority. It seems this outpouring of public anger stem from a genuine grass roots, popular anger. One that the party is eager to take part in even if doubts remain among the leadership if it will amount to much. The party's deployment of its agents are expected to be most influential in the southern parts of the League where their hold remains strong (if waning). As violence flares, hope is renewed in MinGan.
In the fields of Jiangxi, shall the people rise.
Harken the calls to a general strike in Fujian!
The Wuhu Massacre
200 dead. 800 wounded. The news came quickly into Nanchang and Xiamen, disseminating across Fujian and Jiangxi before League authorities could even try to censor it. As striking workers amassed in German factories in Anhui province, their demonstrations were joined by a growing number of protestors that flooded the streets. The police, reinforced by German-trained soldiers, fired upon the crowd.\n\nThe numbers seem to multiply every time the story is retold from person to person, and tales of German advisors deliberately ordering the shootings have spread as well. The end result has been the same, with protests growing in size and numbers and the crisis showing little signs of abating. What began as a protest against German economic overreach has exploded into broader calls for social change, ranging from the abolition of the monarchy, to the elimination of concessionism, to the overthrow of warlords, to the unification of the country, and to the end of capitalism.\n\nMany of the protestors shout to no one in particular, venting their frustrations even though they hold little hope much will be done in a stagnant, divided China. But for the Kuomintang, the moment is nigh. A powder-keg has been set off, and not simply one of anti-concessionism. A propaganda offensive has already gone underway, casting them as heroes in China's hour of need. But there are many promises in the air, and the Kuomintang are hardly the only ones making them.
Moderate positions to create a broader appeal.
Harden opinions to show sincere dedication.
Black Monday and the Red Tide
A whole other world away, the fallout of Germany's economic collapse (already nicknamed Black Monday) has quickly reached China due to extensive German economic presence. Stockbrokers and traders watched with horror as the Shanghai Stock Exchange began closing at record numbers unseen since Shanghai was shaken by the financial tumult of 1925, and local institutions are doing what they can to mitigate the damage.\n\nTo many Kuomintang leaders in Paris, especially figures such as Chen Gongbo and Shi Cuntong, the financial chaos of Black Monday is exactly as Marx predicted: the beginning of possibly a new order, one free from the insatiable greed of capitalism. KMT and LCS cells buzz with activity, mobilising sympathetic unions and other workers' organisations in major cities. The League of Eight Provinces' authority is rapidly eroding, as exemplified by Anqing's break from Nanjing. A recent naval mutiny in Fujian has likewise spurred interest in Paris and Wang Jingwei has ordered the build up of resources in India.\n\nHidden away in the hills and forests of the MinGan Insurgent Zone, Song Qingling and her government have amassed considerable independence from the Central Committee in Paris. Communication between the two Kuomintang governments is limited, and most of the day-to-day operations of the insurgency are led by Song's lieutenants. Among her most trusted military commanders are Generals Li Jishen and Deng Yanda, who believe that the nightmare of Zhili authority over eastern China is finally at an end.\n\nArguing that the time is ripe, Deng has advocated for a quick offensive, positioning well-prepared and trusted militia columns for a surgical strike to be carried out with minimal delay. Li Jishen and others, however, have advocated taking some time to coordinate with groups more loyal to Paris as well as rally previously disillusioned or sleeper cells. Time is of the essence, though the most opportune window is unclear. MinGan's leadership weigh their options...
Take the time to consolidate our forces.
It is coming finally!
The Smiling Tiger Downed
There is nothing perhaps more dutiful and patriotic than Shi Jianqiao's act of filial piety in avenging the death of her father Shi Congbin. Disguised as a serving woman, the young Shi Jianqiao shot the despicable warlord from behind with three bullets from a Browning pistol. While her fate after being arrested by Sun's bodyguards is unknown, the League's former leader now lies in a coma and it is clear that the fragile unity of the League of Eight Provinces is finally coming undone. Urgent messages have flown from the MinGan Insurgency to Shanghai and then to Paris: a final uprising is underway.\n\nWith communications delayed, there is little time to wait for a response. Discussions are underway on whether or not to commit every man to the front-lines of the forthcoming battle or to keep some in reserve. While the guerillas have proved effective in disrupting League control in MinGan, they have not always been particularly effective in the field - especially in pitched, conventional battles. Planners have argued that leaving some as flying columns will allow for logistical flexibility and reinforcements as the campaign unfolds.\n\nOthers warn however that this campaign is do or die, and this will likely be the last chance for socialism to organically take root. Holding back some units will encourage all the disparate cells to hold back for an imaginary fallback position, one that will hardly exist should this operation fail. This fateful choice may very well determine if Dr. Sun's vision can finally be realised.
We need all hands in the fight.
We need a mobile reserve.

A difficult decision needs to be made about how to best address the needs of the countryside.

Friends on the Other Side
Years ago, just outside of Lingyin temple near Hangzhou, a young man was bathing naked on the banks of the West Lake. A pack of nearby school children rushed over to take his discarded clothing, only to be stopped by their young teacher who noticed the bather lacked swimwear. The bather thanked the teacher, and both men readily became friends - both grew up in Zhejiang, were trained to be educators, and above all shared an ambition to have more in life.\n\nThat is the (fanciful) story Dai Chunfeng tells people, for how he was rescued from embarrassment by Hu Zongnan. The Kuomintang Asks for Aid!
Since the National Revolutionary Army collapsed at the hands of the imperialist-backed Zhili Clique, we have certainly looked at the possibility of revolution in China with interest. China, while indeed not a capitalistic nation nor an industrial one, holds the potential for an anti-imperialist and socialist revolution, as evident by the role of the Chinese mass movement in the Northern Expedition.\n\nWhile Chinese socialists and the Kuomintang attempted to stage a bold but failed uprising in 1932, it would appear that following the collapse of the capitalistic world order after Black Monday - the Chinese Kuomintang and the NRA have risen once more to break their chains. We have received an urgent communique from our Chinese connections, such as Chairman Wang Jingwei and ambassador Eugene Chen for our nation to send over military arms and advisors to help the Kuomintang in their renewed revolutionary struggle. We can certainly support them, although, given the distance of the conflict and our limited resources, we can either send them purely advisors or both advisors and rifles. Alternatively, some in our government have argued that instead, we should only send them our thoughts and prayers.

Collapse of the NRA
For years, the NRA had been fighting a war of resistance against the corrupt capitalistic imperialists of the League of Eight Provinces following the failure of the Northern Expedition. While the NRA launched a second abortive uprising in 1932, for many - a new opportunity came with the collapse of the league during the arrival of Black Monday in China.\n\nNonetheless, despite the valiant attempts of the NRA to defeat their enemies in the chaotic League War, it would appear that the strength and morale of the National Revolutionary Army has effectively been crushed on the battlefield. Return of the Central Committee
After a long and tension-filled voyage, the flotilla of ships from the Internationale finally arrived in China. In a daring operation, using a mixture of subterfuge and apt planning, they successfully evaded interception by hostile ships in part because of the ongoing fallout of the mutiny in Mawei and the recent defection of critical Fujian naval forces led by Chen Shaokuan and Chen Jiliang.\n\nAt long last, the Central Committee is able to step foot on Chinese soil once more since their exile in 1927. Owing to the ongoing fighting near the recently secured port of Xiamen, Wang Jingwei kept his remarks brief and with little pomp, though the mood at the ceremony was nonetheless one of great excitement. He and other members of the Paris-based committee quickly met with the leaders of MinGan to establish a working government, and have been remarkably amiable with one another despite lingering differences.\n\nAlso disembarking is a formation of European-trained Chinese forces, carrying a sizeable amount of successfully transported artillery. Trained overseas in their Whampoa-in-exile, they are led by Deputy Headmaster Zhang Zhizhong, Director of the Political Department Zhou Enlai, and Director of the Training Department Hu Zongnan. The last officer of note is Admiral Li Zhilong, who has been commended for his capable naval leadership throughout the operation.
Welcome back Chairman Wang!
Incidents in Wenzhou
Occupation plans for Wenzhou and the other AOG ports have been severely lacking compared to the meticulous steps and lines of advance drawn around Xiamen. When NRA forces occupied the city of Wenzhou, spontaneous anti-foreign riots began all across the city, leading to the murders of numerous German residents and the looting of much of the city's uptown districts. To complicate matters, several smaller advance groups of Nationalist troops also participated in the looting until more disciplined units arrived to secure the area. Wenzhou is now significantly damaged from the civil unrest.
Another mess for our foreign secretary to sort out.
Tragedy in Nantong
The port of Nantong had been leased by the League of Eight Provinces to the AOG, and its position at the mouth of the Yangtze allowed it to act as a German-exclusive alternative to the International City of Shanghai. The advancement of the NRA towards the treaty port caused mass panic and unrest among many of its residents. Widespread looting by Chinese natives combined with scorched-earth tactics by German security forces have lit up the sky above Nantong, and the ensuing fires have wiped out many of the textile factories. An exodus of ferries heading south towards Shanghai were overcrowded and unsuited to trips outside the Yangtze, leading to several of the boats capsizing with hundreds of deaths reported. Before the NRA could do anything to control the situation, it became clear that Nantong was a disaster area. Long seen as an exemplar of how Chinese cities could be modernised, Nantong has effectively been sacked.
A great loss for the country.
Fujianese in Hangzhou
Most of the National Revolutionary Army's first units were raised in Fujian Province from local peasants and the rare urban native, and few if any of these regular troops are familiar with the standard Mandarin dialect. Yesterday a group of Fujianese soldiers on leave in Hangzhou caused a scene when language difficulties and drunkenness led to a fight with local Hangzhou residents. Despite the view of China as one nation, language difficulties and the sharp contrast between rural and urban lifestyles will make stationing most units outside of their home areas difficult.

A New Dawn in Nanjing
Nanjing has been liberated. Gone are the warlords, Sun Chuanfang and Qi Xieyuan, the tyrants who stole from the people and sold the city to Imperialists. At long last, the White Sun flies above the city - the dream of the Northern Expedition nearly a decade ago. In a speech today following the city's capture, a triumphant ceremony honoured the late party founder and all the revolutionary martyrs that have fallen over the years.\n\nMore practically, it is clear that the Kuomintang intend to turn Nanjing into their provisional capital for the duration of the national revolution. Already, the former Governor-General's palace (and the same building where Dr. Sun was sworn in as provisional president in 1911) has been converted into a provisional Presidential Palace.\n\nA provisional Executive Yuan is being established as well, subordinate to the Central Executive Committee, with Wang Jingwei as the President of the National Government. Liao Zhongkai has been appointed Premier of the Executive Yuan, a new position to serve as head of the Kuomintang government. It appears that Kuomintang have begun their first forays into ruling an organised state.

Kuomintang Exiles Arrive in Shaanxi
For the past four years, Kuomintang forces under the reorganised National Revolutionary Army had been fighting a brutal guerrila war against the League of Eight Provinces in the Min-Gan Insurgency zone between the regions of Fujian and Jiangxi. Despite a valiant uprising following the new year, it appears that once more the Kuomintang finds itself on the run and that the Second National Revolutionary Army was unable to complete the mission set out by its predecessors.\n\nAs Kuomintang politicians and officers flee across the country or for abroad for their second-largest exile since the collapse of the Northern Expedition, tattered remains of the insurgent zone including several well-trained officers such as Lin Biao and Xu Xiangqian have managed to traverse across the country and have arrived to the border of Shanaxi province to seek asylum and have pledged their loyalty to Shanxi's provincial armies. They are also joined by RCA politicians and intellectuals who have long links with Shanxi's revolutionary cadre and will no doubt seek to continue on the legacy of Dr. Sun in Shaanxi Province. While adding these valiant soldiers to our forces could bolster our ranks with experienced and veteran officers, there is also the concern that these Kuomintang exiles may carry radical teachings and it may be advisable that we keep our borders secure and our people safe from radicalism.

Victory in the League War
For many outside observers of the tumultuous Chinese political situation since the 1911 Xinhai Revolution, the Chinese Nationalist Party's pursuits of national unification were thoroughly quashed with the failure of the Northern Expedition. The Kuomintang movement, which splintered into competing factions, seemed destined for failure.\n\nFollowing the collapse of Zhili authority in the League of Eight Provinces following Black Monday; it would appear that the Kuomintang has surpassed these odds and has re-emerged as a vibrant political force. Years of biding their time in Europe and the MinGan Insurgent Zone has bore fruit, as guerrilla soldiers and militia of the resurgent National Revolutionary Army have won victory after victory against their adversaries. With the conflict's conclusion in Eastern China, the time has come to rebuild the provinces and heal from the scars of war. For observers within the Internationale, it would appear that their sponsorship of the Kuomintang has finally yielded its reward, as calls have gone out to rally the Kuomintang movement once more to unify and save China from her strife.

Having been ousted from the politics of China for more than a decade now, the Kuomintang's recent victory over its enemies in the League War has seen Sun Yat-sen's idea for a national revolution revived once more. Once the home of the Ming emperors, the Provisional Presidential Palace (which had been used as the seat of power for Sun Chuanfang's autocratic rule over the Eight Provinces) - has now been renovated into the Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Government. News of the Kuomintang's First Repatriated Congress is beginning to spread across China, rallying like-minded revolutionaries in a common goal to fulfil the dream of the Northern Expedition and create a modern and just Republic of China.\n\nIn addition, a delegation from the Third Internationale will also be in attendance at the Congress. Having long pledged their support to the Kuomintang since the Party's initial reorganisation in 1924, the Central Committee has long played exile in Paris and owes its remarkable success to the backing of the two major syndicalist nations of Europe. The Closing of the Congress
After several weeks of long deliberations, the First Repatriated Congress of the Kuomintang has formally adjourned. Although much had been decided upon, there were plenty left unresolved and subtle fractures have begun to form between Wang's loyalists and his divided opposition. In the meantime, as delegates and representatives prepare to head on home, they have decided to entrust the third and latest Central Executive Committee to manage party affairs.\n\nHeaded by Chairman Wang Jingwei and Vice Chairman Liao Zhongkai, the two are joined by twenty-two others: Bai Yunti, Chen Gongbo, Chen Youren, Deng Yanda, Dong Biwu, Gu Mengyu, Li Jishen, Lin Boqu, Liang Hancao, Pan Yunchao, Peng Zemin, Shi Cuntong, Song Qingling, Song Ziwen, Sun Fo, Wang Faqin, Wu Chaoshu, Xu Deheng, Zhang Bojun, Zhang Yunchuan, Zeng Xing, and Zhu Jiqing.\n\nGiven disciplinary powers and with say over financial affairs is the Central Supervisory Committee, made up of Kuomintang stalwarts Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, Xu Qian and Zhang Renjie. Both committees also have extensive and carefully negotiated alternative member rosters.\n\nA delicate balance of power has been erected, with Wang and his RCA carefully moving to consolidate his government without provoking excessive backlash from those increasingly antagonised by his efforts to assert his authority. Perhaps best encapsulating the emerging power games being played is Wang's decision to appoint Sun Fo as Vice Premier of the Executive Yuan (a new prestigious but rather powerless position), to help remove a rival from loyalist Chen Gongbo's bid to become Premier of the Legislative Yuan. Although the full cabinet is yet to be named, Song Qingling and her PAC allies are said to be already grumbling about a lack of representation, feeling deliberately locked out, however it is unlikely that they can do much to contest the President's appointments.

The Death of Liao Zhongkai
Tragedy struck the Kuomintang last week, as one of its pivotal figures is laid to rest. Liao Zhongkai was a founding member of the Kuomintang and at least titularly the second highest ranking member of the party-state. Widely respected among the left, he has continued to nurse lasting wounds from a brutal assassination attempt in 1925. It seems that he has finally succumbed to those wounds, though thankfully lived long enough to see the party return from its exile.\n\nAs his funeral concludes near Nanjing, his personal effects are not the only things being divided. Following a tradition set by Dr. Sun himself, his wife He Xiangning (herself a prominent revolutionary) has taken his Central Executive Committee seat. The position of Vice Chairman of the CEC, a position specially created for him during the exile period, has gone to Song Qingling - helping preserve the balance of power within the party.\n\nRemaining in contention however, is the title of Premier of the Executive Yuan. The nominal head of the executive branch, it was freshly created during the League War as a replacement for the old Beiyang prime minister. Liao hardly had any time to utilise it however, leaving executive power effectively in the hands of the nominally weak Presidency. To Wang, the job was meant as a means of personally recognising Liao's contributions. To his rivals in the PAC, it represented a necessary counterweight to the Chairman as Liao was seen as more conciliatory.\n\nWang is determined to avoid having to split executive prerogatives, fearing the perils of a powerless President vulnerable to political machinations. As President of the Republic, it is in his right to appoint the Premier, and Chen Gongbo is the most logical candidate. A loyal protege, friend, and the leader of the RCA, his candidacy is troubled by his personal radicalism and the fact that Wang needs him elsewhere. The alternative is for Wang to abolish the Premiership and incorporate it into the Presidency, certain to cause alarm. Whatever he decides, his choice will cast a long shadow, setting a precedent for the future for Presidential-Premier relationships in the Republic.

The Divided Sister Party
As the largest faction and movement within the League of Chinese Syndicalists, the Chinese Syndicalist Party boasts the most union membership and followers in China. With inspiration from the glorious revolutions of Britain and France following the Great War, the Old Guard of the Chinese Syndicalists such as party members Chen Duxiu, Li Lisan, and Liu Shaoqi believe that in order for the proletarian socialist revolution to happen - the national revolution must be won first. When the Kuomintang was reorganised in 1924, the syndicalists and the Kuomintang worked together in a pledge of unity - the so called United Front.\n\nIdeally the Orthodox Syndicalists of the CSP envision a system akin to the Commune of France, with unions and councils working together in tandem. The ongoing civic and political turmoil of the French state however has led to doubts towards the leadership of the orthodox CSP. Moves and Countermoves
The hound has long slipped from its leash, a fact that many within the Kuomintang central leadership have come to regret. The National Revolutionary Army, a force designed specifically to protect the party from warlord and military control, has slowly developed a mind of its own, and rumours of military conspiracies swirl as each faction courts sympathetic officers.\n\nWang Jingwei is no stranger to this threat, and neither are those closest to him. Although Wang has substantial control over the bureaucracy, the support of at the least plurality of intellectuals and Chen Gongbo has whipped his RCA into a disciplined (albeit unofficial) caucus, his position at the top of the party has never felt quite secure.\n\nHis wife, Chen Bijun, has a plan. A determined woman, with painful memories of the power-struggle her husband had with Chiang Kai-shek, knows all too well the power of the military in dictating party priorities. She has independently begun the legwork for creating a pro-Chairman military faction, something that she has finally informed Wang in detail. With the help of Zhang Zhizhong, Zhou Enlai, and the advisors of the MMIC, she has drafted a list of members of the Political Department, the European-trained syndicalist officers, and other young guard loyalists to install into key positions in the NRA hierarchy.\n\nSuch blatant meddling in the army might be just enough to bring the military to heel, breaking their independent political spirit. On the other hand, Wang is hesitant despite Chen's rosy outlook, noting that many NRA officers are genuinely apolitical and such open demands of political loyalty may backfire by driving them into the opposition. Chen's open efforts to install her brother Chen Changzu as a general in the air force has caused plenty of blowback in the past. Presenting an image of being a respectable statesman above such petty bickering might be the better route to keep his power. Then again, revolution is often a dirty business and as President and Commander-in-Chief it is his right to grant military commissions. Perhaps it is better to be feared than overthrown.
